On a failure, the target can’t take any actions and is helpless until the start of the dragon’s next turn as its limbs become paralyzed. On a success, the target is dazed until the end of its next turn</p><p><b>C: Ice breath +11 vs. PD (1d4 nearby enemies in a group)</b> — 10 cold damage, and the closest target hit is dazed until the start of the dragon’s next turn<br> <i>Miss:</i> Half damage.</p><p><i>Evasive turn:</i> Once per battle as a free action when an attack targets the dragon, it can force the attacker to reroll the attack and has <i>resist damage 12+</i> against that attack.</p><p><i>Resist cold 12+:</i> When a cold attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 12+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>90</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Dragon, Other

### Shadow Dragon

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>8<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Caster</b></p><p><b>Dragon</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +13</p><p><b>Shadow claws +13 vs. AC</b> — 50 psychic damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The target is confused (hard save ends, 16+).</p><p><b>C: Nightmare breath +12 vs. MD (1d3 nearby or far away enemies)</b> — 60 negative energy damage, and the target becomes a living shadow (hard save ends, 16+)<br> <i>Living shadow:</i> While a living shadow, the target can’t physically interact with or gain aid from companions or aid them (including healing, bonuses, and effects) but is otherwise “normal”.<br> <i>Limited use:</i> 1/battle, but the ability recharges when the dragon is staggered. If it hasn’t already made a <i>nightmare breath</i> attack when it becomes staggered, the dragon makes the attack as a free action and then the breath recharges.</p><p><i>Made of shadow:</i> The shadow dragon perceives the invisible, is unaffected by the <i>blur</i> spell, and ignores illusions. Rogues attempting to <i>shadow walk</i> near a shadow dragon end up in the dragon’s belly (save ends). While there, they are helpless and take 2d12 damage at the start of each of their turns until they save and fall back out of shadow.</p><p><i>Shadowy escalation:</i> When in poorly lit areas of shadow, the dragon adds the escalation die to its attack rolls. Complete darkness or bright daylight negates the ability.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Shadow illusions:</i> As a standard action, the dragon can appear to be humanoid, usually disguising itself as an unthreatening old man in a cloak (DC 35 to detect). Daylight will show the illusion for what it is — an insubstantial dragon. Dragons with a <i>Book of Many Faces</i> will have perfect humanoid disguises. Dropping the illusion is a free action.</p><p><i>Shadowy phasing:</i> When the escalation die is even, natural odd attack rolls against the dragon automatically miss. When the escalation die is odd, natural even attack rolls against the dragon automatically miss. Attacks that deal holy damage ignore this ability.</p><p><span>On Holy Ground</span></p><p>While on “holy ground” such as a temple or consecrated shrine, all hard saves against shadow dragon effects become normal saves. As a standard action, a cleric who invokes the gods can produce a similar anti-shadow effect in the nearby area until the start of their next turn, or they can turn hard saves against shadow dragon abilities to easy saves if that area is already on holy ground. Shadow dragons try to avoid holy ground, and shadow thieves can only enter it while possessing victims and will flee once the possession ends. It’s up to the GM what counts as “holy ground” in their game.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>25</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>260</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Shadow Thief

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>8<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Dragon</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +17</p><p><b>Shadow strangulation +13 vs. PD</b> — 20 psychic damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The target takes 20 negative energy damage, and the shadow thief can make a <i>shadow possession</i> attack as a free action (but see <i>group ability</i>).</p><p><i>[Group ability]</i> <b>C: Shadow possession +13 vs. MD (one enemy hit by <i>shadow strangulation</i>)</b> — The shadow thief “crawls inside” the target. The target is confused (save ends), and the shadow thief can’t be the target of an attack or effect until it’s forced from the target’s body when that creature saves against the confusion effect.</p><p><i>Group ability:</i> For every four shadow thieves in the battle (round up), one of them can use <i>shadow possession</i> during the battle.</p><p><i>Shadow thievery:</i> The shadow thief is an extension of the shadow dragon, not really a separate entity. When it drops to 0 hp, it flees back to the shadow dragon and merges with it. When this happens, if there is at least one enemy engaged with that shadow thief, the thief chooses one enemy engaged with it. Roll a d20; on a 16+, the shadow thief steals a random magic item from the chosen enemy as it flees back to the dragon (but see <i>stop…thief</i> below). Stolen items are replaced with shadowy duplicates that work until the end of the battle then fade to nothingness. The items can be recovered if the dragon is slain in the same battle.</p><p><i>Stop…thief!</i> When a shadow thief steals an item, the creature it steals from can choose to prevent the theft, but at a cost. If the natural d20 thievery roll was odd, the target of the thievery attempt can choose to keep the item but become hampered (save ends) as they wrestle with the shadow. If the natural thievery roll was even, the target has the same choice, but it’s a hard save (16+) to end the hampered effect.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>25</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>38</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Drider

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>6<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Caster</b></p><p><b>Aberration</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +10</p><p><b>Sword or mace +9 vs. AC</b> — 20 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The drider can make a <i>poison bite</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>Poison bite +9 vs. PD</b> — 10 poison damage, and 10 ongoing poison damage</p><p><b>R: Lightning bolt spell +11 vs. PD</b> — 30 lightning damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The drider can make a <i>lightning bolt spell</i> attack against a second nearby enemy, followed by a third and final different nearby enemy if the second attack is also a natural even hit.</p><p><b>C: Web attack +11 vs. PD (up to 2 nearby enemies in a group)</b> — The target is hampered (save ends)<br> <i>Limited use:</i> 1/round as a quick action, if the escalation die is even.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>170</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Drow

Drow may optionally include one of these abilities as nastier specials: _Drow Cruelty_ or _Poisons and Potions_.

Drow Cruelty

Choose one of the following abilities for all non-mook drow in a battle to have:

_Poisoner:_ When the drow scores a critical hit, it can forego damage to force the target to start making last gasp saves. On the fourth failure, the target falls unconscious (and can’t be woken normally) for 2d4 minutes.

_Take advantage of weakness:_ Whenever an enemy nearby a drow rolls a save, it takes its level in damage.

_Umbral caul:_ As long as at least one drow uses a standard action each round to maintain the supernatural darkness, each non-drow creature in the battle becomes dazed (save ends) whenever it rolls a natural 1–5 with an attack roll.

_Venomous:_ The first time each battle a drow hits with a weapon attack, the target also takes 5 ongoing poison damage.

Poisons and Potions

Drinking a potion, applying a poison, or using a substance requires only a quick action for a drow with one of these options. Characters who acquire any of these drow items must use a standard action to drink/apply them.

_Draft of Eschaton_ (potion): When drunk it immediately purges the body of all poisons and toxins and ends any ongoing conditions. All the drinker’s saves (including last gasp saves and death saves) automatically succeed for the rest of the battle or for five minutes. Immediately after the battle, the drinker must make a DC 30 Constitution check or be completely debilitated and unable to travel far or to fight for a day.

_Dragon Apples:_ Small ceramic spheres that explode. Make a basic ranged attack against a nearby enemy (or level + 5 for drow); on a hit, the target takes 10 ongoing fire damage.

_Midnight Tincture:_ When this glass vial is broken, the nearby area is shrouded in clinging darkness. The darkness lasts 3 rounds. Each creature in the darkness except drow takes a –4 attack penalty. The tincture can be attached to an arrow or bolt.

_Potion of Spider Climbing:_ For one battle or five minutes the drinker can climb on ceilings and walls as easily as it moves on the ground.

_Spider Venom:_ A creature hit by a melee weapon coated in the venom takes 5 ongoing poison damage when the attack roll is a natural 16+.

_Web Dust:_ Made from desiccated spiders, this dust can hold a door shut or stick an object to a wall for five minutes. Champion-tier creatures can make a DC 20 skill check to rip through something held by _web dust_ before it fully dissolves, and epic-tier creatures can rip through such objects in a round. Further applications increase the effectiveness: three applications lasts for fifteen minutes, requires 3 successful checks, and takes 3 rounds for epic-tier characters to get through.

### Drow Darkbolt

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>7<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Archer</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +12</p><p><b>Dagger and spidersilk line +12 vs. AC (one nearby enemy)</b> — 22 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 8 damage.</p><p><b>R: Exsanguinating barbed arrows +12 vs. AC (one nearby or far away enemy)</b> — 20 damage, and 6 ongoing damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> As a free action, the darkbolt can make a second <i>barbed arrows</i> attack against a different enemy with a –2 attack penalty. If it gets another natural even hit, it can make a third (and final) <i>barbed arrows</i> attack against a different enemy with a –4 attack penalty as a free action.</p><p><i>Darkbolt vanish!:</i> If unengaged, when the darkbolt attacks and rolls a natural even miss, it can step into a shadow-dimension that turn as a move action. While in the shadows, it can’t be seen or targeted with attacks, and it reappears anywhere nearby at the start of its next turn.</p><p><i>Wall-crawler:</i> A darkbolt can climb on ceilings and walls as easily as it moves on the ground thanks to its rope-dagger and spiked bracers.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Well equipped:</i> The drow has a potion or poison that it can use as a quick action twice this battle (see Drow Abilities).</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>100</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Elder Beast

### Hagunemnon

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>13<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Aberration</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +16</p><p><b>Spontaneous metamorphosing limbs +18 vs. AC</b> — 110 damage, and the hagunemnon can make a <i>spontaneous metamorphosing limbs</i> attack against a different target as a free action<br> <i>Natural 19+:</i> The target starts making last gasp saves. On the fourth failure, it becomes a shapeless ooze.<br> <i>Diminishing limbs:</i> With each subsequent hit after the first, <i>spontaneous metamorphosing limbs</i> deals 20 less damage. The hagunemnon also doesn’t gain any extra attacks when it makes a basic attack.</p><p><i>Dimension hop:</i> As a move action when the escalation die is odd, the hagunemnon can teleport nearby or far away to a location it can see.</p><p><i>Resist psychic 18+:</i> When a psychic attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 18+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><i>Shapechange:</i> As a standard action, the hagunemnon can change its form to that of any large or medium creature, or back to its own shape. Seeing through the shapechange requires a DC 25 skill check.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Madness aura:</i> When a creature is engaged with the hagunemnon at the start of its turn, it takes 4d10 psychic damage. If it takes 31 or more damage this way during a single turn, it’s also confused until the start of its next turn.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>29</b></p><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>27</b></p><p><b>864</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Umluppuk

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Huge</b></p><p><b>7<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Aberration</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +15</p><p><b>Pods of mouths and eyes +12 vs. AC (4 attacks)</b> — 20 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target is stuck (easy save ends, 6+).<br> <i>Miss:</i> 10 damage.</p><p><b>C: Chorus of madness +12 vs. MD (up to 3 random nearby creatures)</b> — 10 ongoing psychic damage, and the target is confused (save ends both)<br> <i>Quick use:</i> This ability only requires a quick action (once per round) instead of a standard action when the umluppuk starts its turn unengaged (or without an enemy consumed if you are using the nastier special!).</p><p><i>Resist psychic 18+:</i> When a psychic attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 18+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Consume:</i> Once per round during its turn, the umluppuk can make a <i>consume</i> attack against a stuck enemy as a quick action. The umluppuk can only have one target consumed at a time.</p><p><b>Consume +12 vs. PD (one stuck enemy)</b> — 50 damage, and the target takes 10 ongoing acid damage and is absorbed into the umluppuk (hard save ends both, 16+); while inside the umluppuk, the target is vulnerable to the umluppuk’s <i>pods of mouths and eyes</i> attacks (<i>attacks vs. it have crit range expanded by 2</i>), and it’s stuck.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>310</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Warped Beast

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Aberration</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9</p><p><b>Tentacle maw +10 vs. AC</b> — 16 damage<br> <i>Natural 18+:</i> The target is hampered until the end of its next turn.<br> <i>Miss:</i> The warped beast can make a <i>psychic blast</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: Psychic blast +10 vs. MD (1d3 nearby enemies)</b> — 8 psychic damage<br> <i>Natural 18+:</i> The target is confused until the end of its next turn.</p><p><i>One madness feature:</i> At the start of each of the warped beast’s turns, roll a d6. The warped beast gains the corresponding ability until the start of its next turn.</p><p><i>1. Amorphous oozing form:</i> The beast has <i>resist damage 11+</i> to all damage.</p><p><i>2. Dimensional slide:</i> Once during its turn, the warped beast can teleport anywhere nearby it can see as a move action. Each enemy engaged with it when it teleports is confused until the end of its next turn.</p><p><i>3. Fear aura:</i> While engaged with the warped beast, enemies that have 24 hp or fewer are dazed (–4 attack) and do not add the escalation die to their attacks.</p><p><i>4. Gibbering mouths:</i> When an enemy ends its turn engaged with the warped beast, it’s confused until the end of its next turn.</p><p><i>5. Many spontaneous limbs:</i> When the warped beast makes a <i>tentacle maw</i> attack during its turn, roll a d4. That many additional limbs or tentacles spontaneously erupt from the creature and make an additional basic attack that turn (special abilities/effects don’t trigger on those extra attacks). Each of those attacks only deals half damage.</p><p><i>6. Warping touch:</i> When the warped beast hits a creature with a <i>tentacle maw</i> attack, the target also takes 5 ongoing psychic damage and a –2 penalty to saves (save ends both).</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Warped mutant:</i> Roll two madness features instead of one each round (reroll similar results).</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>75</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Elemental

### Air Elemental

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Elemental</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +11</p><p><b>Slam +10 vs. AC</b> — 12 damage</p><p><b>C: Swirling winds +10 vs. PD (1d3 random nearby conscious enemies)</b> — 14 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target pops free from the elemental.</p><p><i>Flight:</i> It’s quick and lively.</p><p><i>Resist non-spell damage 16+:</i> When a non-spell attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 16+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><i>Whirlwind transformation:</i> Roll a d10 at the start of each of the air elemental’s turns. If you roll less than or equal to the escalation die, it shifts into whirlwind form until the end of the battle. While in this form it gains the following improved attack (and you stop rolling <i>whirlwind transformation</i> checks):</p><p><b>Elemental whirlwind +10 vs. PD (each enemy engaged with it <i>and</i> one nearby enemy)</b> — 14 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> Half damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>52</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Big Air Elemental

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>7<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Elemental</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +14</p><p><b>Slam +13 vs. AC</b> — 20 damage</p><p><b>C: Swirling winds +13 vs. PD (1d3 random conscious nearby enemies)</b> — 22 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target pops free from the elemental.</p><p><i>Flight:</i> It’s quick and direct.</p><p><i>Resist non-spell damage 16+:</i> When a non-spell attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 16+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><i>Whirlwind transformation:</i> Roll a d8 at the start of each of the air elemental’s turns. If you roll less than or equal to the escalation die, it shifts into whirlwind form until the end of the battle. While in this form it gains the following improved attack (and you stop rolling <i>whirlwind transformation</i> checks):</p><p><b>Elemental whirlwind +13 vs. PD (each enemy engaged with it <i>and</i> one nearby enemy)</b> — 22 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> Half damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>88</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Big Earth Elemental

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>7</b><b>th</b><b> level</b></p><p><b>Blocker</b></p><p><b>Elemental</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9</p><p><b>Rocky fists +11 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 16 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 7 damage.</p><p><i>Boulder up:</i> Roll a d8 at the start of each of the earth elemental’s turns. If you roll less than or equal to the escalation die, it shifts into boulder guardian form until the end of the battle. While in this form, it gains a +2 bonus to AC and the <i>relentless pursuit</i> ability (and you stop rolling <i>boulder up</i> checks).</p><p><i>Relentless pursuit:</i> The elemental must be in boulder guardian form to use this ability. Staggered enemies can’t disengage from the earth elemental. (They can pop free, but they can’t roll disengage checks.)</p><p><i>Repair damage 10 and below:</i> When the earth elemental is targeted by a natural attack roll of 10 or less, the elemental heals 3d6 damage before taking any damage from the attack.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Burrow:</i> Not all earth elementals burrow, though if yours is particularly nasty or associated with a particular icon, it can.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>94</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Big Fire Elemental

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>7<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Elemental</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +13</p><p><b>Whipping flames +12 vs. PD</b> — 22 fire damage, and 11 ongoing fire damage to a random nearby enemy (including an unconscious one)</p><p><i>Melee burn:</i> When an enemy makes a natural odd melee attack roll against the fire elemental, that attacker takes 2d12 fire damage.</p><p><i>Resist fire 18+:</i> When a fire attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 18+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><i>Wildfire transformation:</i> Roll a d8 at the start of each of the fire elemental’s turns. If you roll less than or equal to the escalation die, it shifts into wildfire form until the end of the battle. While in this form, it gains the following improved attack (and you stop rolling <i>wildfire transformation</i> checks):</p><p><b>C: Elemental wildfire +12 vs. PD (one nearby enemy OR each nearby enemy taking ongoing fire damage)</b> — 30 fire damage, and 11 ongoing fire damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 11 ongoing fire damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>92</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Big Water Elemental

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>7<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Blocker</b></p><p><b>Elemental</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +11</p><p><b>Surge +11 vs. AC (up to 2 enemies)</b> — 22 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> The elemental heals 9 hp.</p><p><i>Great wave transformation:</i> Roll a d8 at the start of each of the water elemental’s turns. If you roll less than or equal to the escalation die, it shifts into great wave form until the end of the battle. While in this form, each enemy engaged with the elemental is hampered (and you stop rolling <i>great wave transformation</i> checks).</p><p><i>Liquid empowerment:</i> The water elemental gains a +2 bonus to attacks and all defenses while it’s in contact with a body of water, or while it’s nearby a sizeable body of water. A bucket or a bathtub of liquid doesn’t count; it must be at least a pond, creek, or maybe a large fountain. If the water elemental moves far away from the body of water the empowerment ends.</p><p><i>Resist weapon damage 16+:</i> When a weapon attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 16+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>100</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Earth Elemental

If you roll less than or equal to the escalation die, it shifts into boulder guardian form until the end of the battle. While in this form, it gains a +2 bonus to AC and the <i>relentless pursuit</i> ability (and you stop rolling <i>boulder up</i> checks).</p><p><i>Relentless pursuit:</i> The elemental must be in boulder guardian form to use this ability. Staggered enemies can’t disengage from the earth elemental. (They can pop free, but they can’t roll disengage checks.)</p><p><i>Repair damage 10 and below:</i> When the earth elemental is targeted by a natural attack roll of 10 or less, the elemental heals 1d12 damage before taking any damage from the attack.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Burrow:</i> Not all earth elementals burrow, though if yours is particularly nasty or associated with a particular icon, it can.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>66</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Epic Earth Elemental

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>9<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Blocker</b></p><p><b>Elemental</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +12</p><p><b>Rocky fists +13 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 28 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 14 damage.</p><p><i>Boulder up:</i> Roll a d6 at the start of each of the earth elemental’s turns. If you roll less than or equal to the escalation die, it shifts into boulder guardian form until the end of the battle. While in this form, it gains a +2 bonus to AC and the <i>relentless pursuit</i> ability (and you stop rolling <i>boulder up</i> checks).</p><p><i>Relentless pursuit:</i> The elemental must be in boulder guardian form to use this ability. Staggered enemies can’t disengage from the earth elemental. (They can pop free, but they can’t roll disengage checks.)</p><p><i>Repair damage 10 and below:</i> When the earth elemental is targeted by a natural attack roll of 10 or less, the elemental heals 5d6 damage before taking any damage from the attack.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Burrow:</i> Not all earth elementals burrow, though if yours is particularly nasty or associated with a particular icon, it can.</p><p><i>Endless vitality:</i> When an enemy engaged with the epic earth elemental heals using one or more recoveries, the elemental heals 5d6 hit points.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>25</b></p><p><b>24</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>170</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Epic Fire Elemental

This one can, and it only touches the ground to set something ablaze.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>24</b></p><p><b>24</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>166</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Small Water Elemental

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Blocker</b></p><p><b>Elemental</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +7</p><p><b>Surge +7 vs. AC (up to 2 enemies)</b> — 8 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> The elemental heals 3 hp.</p><p><i>Liquid empowerment:</i> The water elemental gains a +2 bonus to attacks and all defenses while it’s in contact with a body of water, or while it’s nearby a sizeable body of water. A bucket or a bathtub of liquid doesn’t count; it must be at least a pond, creek, or maybe a large fountain. If the water elemental moves far away from the body of water the empowerment ends.</p><p><i>Resist weapon damage 16+:</i> When a weapon attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 16+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>12</b></p><p><b>40</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

While in this form, each enemy engaged with the elemental is hampered (and you stop rolling <i>great wave transformation</i> checks).</p><p><i>Liquid empowerment:</i> The water elemental gains a +2 bonus to attacks and all defenses while it’s in contact with a body of water, or while it’s nearby a sizeable body of water. ## Flower of Unlife

Nastier Specials for all flowers of unlife

_Iconic energy draing:_ When a PC is associated with an icon that is also associated with the flower of unlife (e.g. undead or nature icons), and they roll a natural 1–5 with an attack against the flower, the attacker takes 2d6 damage and the flower heals that many hit points.

### Blood Rose

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>2×</b></p><p><b>6<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Plant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +10<br>Vulnerability: fire</p><p><b>Fangs in the blossoms +11 vs. AC</b> — 20 damage<br> <i>Natural odd hit:</i> The target takes 10 ongoing damage.<br> <i>Natural odd miss:</i> 5 ongoing damage.</p><p><i>Bristling thorns:</i> When a creature makes a melee attack against the blood rose, that creature takes damage equal to its natural attack roll.</p><p><i>Black-gray resurgence:</i> When the blood rose drops to 0 hit points, it is destroyed until the start of its next turn. At the start of its next turn, it returns to life as a death blossom or lich flower that lacks the <i>red-yellow resurrection</i> ability but is otherwise undamaged and whole.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>110</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

Gaining a recovery is not healing, but it can use that recovery later to heal as normal.</p><p><i>Red-yellow resurrection:</i> When the death blossom drops to 0 hit points, it’s destroyed until the start of its next turn. ## Fungaloid

Some fungaloids can make special attacks. For those, add the fungaloid creature’s level to attacks and damage, as indicated.

**C: Poison tentacles 5 + level vs. PD (1d3 nearby enemies)** — 3 + level poison damage, and the target is vulnerable to _fungal attacks_ (save ends)

**C: Brown noise 5 + level vs. PD (1d3 nearby enemies)** — 3 + level ongoing thunder damage

**C: Hallucinogenia 3 + level vs. MD (one nearby enemy)** — The target is confused (easy save ends, 6+)

**C: Infectious spores 5 + level vs. PD (1d3 nearby enemies)** — 3 + level ongoing poison damage

**C: Piercing shriek 5 + level vs. PD (1d3 nearby enemies)** — 4 + level psychic damage

### Aerial Spore

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>2<sup>nd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Plant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +1</p><p><b>C: Stinging tendrils +6 vs. PD (one nearby enemy)</b> — 4 poison damage, and the target is weakened until the end of its next turn</p><p><i>Puffball exploder:</i> The first time each round an aerial spore in the battle drops to 0 hp, it explodes and 1d3 nearby non-fungus non-construct creatures are covered in spores and begin to choke. Until the end of the battle, when a choking creature rolls a natural 1–5 on an attack roll, it takes damage equal to the natural roll. If a creature is affected twice by this attack, the damage it takes on a natural 1–5 doubles; if affected three times, it triples, etc.</p><p><i>Spores:</i> A creature choking from <i>puffball exploder</i> can use a standard action to wash the spores off itself and/or cough them up, preventing further choking effects until it’s affected by <i>puffball exploder</i> again.</p><p><i>Weightless:</i> The aerial spore floats upon air currents, but it prefers to stay within 5 to 7 feet of the ground so it can use its tendrils to keep it in place or propel it. A free-floating spore too far away from the ground to use its tendrils can easily be blown about from strong winds or similar magical effects.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>9</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>7</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

When no enemies are staggered, the braincap uses <i>hallucinogenia</i> if its hit points are even, and <i>psionic filaments</i> if its hit points are odd.</p><p><b>R: Focused brain blast +8 vs. PD (1 nearby or far away staggered enemy)</b> — 21 force damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 5 psychic damage.</p><p><b>C: Hallucinogenia +8 vs. MD (1d3 nearby enemies)</b> — The target is confused (easy save ends, 6+) and vulnerable to psychic damage until the end of the battle<br> <i>Miss:</i> The target sees odd colors at the corners of its vision until it has taken a full heal-up (–2 penalty to skill checks to see things).</p><p><b>C: Psionic filaments +8 vs. MD (1d3 nearby enemies)</b> — 15 psychic damage</p><p><i>Lost opportunity:</i> This creature can’t make opportunity attacks.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>90</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Fungaloid Empress

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Huge</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Plant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +15</p><p><b>Crushing limbs +9 vs. AC (1d3 enemies engaged with the empress)</b> — 18 damage</p><p><i>Combat womb:</i> At the end of each of the empress’ turns, if there are fewer than two elder spores (see below) per enemy, add a number of elder spores to the battle so that there are two spores per enemy. A spore can “sprout” already engaged with a nearby or far away enemy or on its own, it’s up to you.</p><p><i>Sporulating spiracles:</i> Fungus grows on everything in the area! Whenever a non-fungus creature attempts to move, it must make a DC 18 Dexterity or Strength check to do so or it loses its move action. If the creature uses a standard action to clear away fungus, it can move normally that turn.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>170</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Fungaloid Monarch

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>2×</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Leader</b></p><p><b>Plant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +8</p><p><b>Mycotic scepter +9 vs. AC</b> — 24 damage<br> <i>Natural 12+:</i> One nearby fungaloid can make a <i>fungal attack</i> as a free action.<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> Up to three nearby fungaloids can each make a <i>fungal attack</i> as a free action.<br> <i>Natural 20:</i> Up to five nearby fungaloids can each make a <i>fungal attack</i> as a free action.</p><p><i>Group mind:</i> The monarch’s attacks deal +1 damage for each other allied creature with the plant type in the battle (max +10).</p><p><i>Drudge-summons:</i> If there are not enough nearby fungaloids to use up all the <i>fungal attacks</i> granted by the <i>mycotic scepter</i>, skip the extra fungal attacks but add a full-strength fungaloid drudge to the battle next to the fungaloid monarch.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>98</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Sporrior

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>2<sup>nd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Plant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +10</p><p><b>Chitinous bite +7 vs. AC</b> — 5 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The sporrior can make a <i>spore cloud</i> attack this turn as a quick action.</p><p><b>R: Parasitic darts +6 vs. AC (1d3 nearby or far away enemies in a group)</b> — 5 poison damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The sporrior can make a <i>spore cloud</i> attack this turn as a quick action.</p><p><b>C: Spore cloud +6 vs. PD (1d3 nearby enemies)</b> — 4 poison damage</p><p><i>Sprinter:</i> A sporrior gains an extra move action when the escalation die is odd.</p><p><i>Wall-crawler:</i> A sporrior can climb on ceilings and walls as easily as it moves on the ground.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>12</b></p><p><b>36</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Gargoyle

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Troop</b></p><p><b>Construct</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +4</p><p><b>Furious claws and fangs +9 vs. AC</b> — 9 damage<br> <i>Natural 11+:</i> The gargoyle can make two more melee attacks as a free action (but never more than three total attacks per standard action, even if you roll another 11+).</p><p><i>Flight:</i> As the standard monster ability.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Rocky hide:</i> The gargoyle has <i>resist damage 12+</i> against attacks targeting AC.</p><p><i>Statues, statues, everywhere:</i> Because they often look like statues, gargoyles are capable of springing a surprise on inattentive PCs. When there’s a chance of such an ambush, give the PCs a champion-tier skill check (usually DC 20) to notice the gargoyles and avoid being surprised.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>24</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>60</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Gelahedron

For special abilities, see Ooze Abilities.

### Gelatinous Cubahedron (aka Cube)

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Huge</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Blocker</b></p><p><b>Ooze</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +4</p><p><b>Shlup’n’schlorp +10 vs. PD</b> — 30 acid damage, and the cube engulfs the target (functions like a grab; see below) if it’s smaller than the cube<br> <i>Miss:</i> The cube can make a <i>spasms </i>attack as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: Spasms +10 vs. AC (up to 2 attacks, each against a different nearby enemy)</b> — 15 damage</p><p><i>Engulf and dissolve:</i> Targets engulfed/grabbed by the cube take 30 acid damage at the start of the cube’s turn but are not viable targets for additional attacks by the cube. Multiple targets can be held within the cube simultaneously.<br> Any engulfed creature that is also staggered must begin making last gasp saves or become paralyzed as the cube’s toxins overwhelm it.</p><p><i>Instinctive actions:</i> Gelatinous creatures have no brains, sometimes they just <i>do things</i>. When the escalation die is odd, instead of making an attack or moving, roll a d6 to see what the cubahedron does. If an option is not viable (you roll a 5 but there is no engulfed enemy), reroll until you get a valid option.</p><p><b>1.</b> The cubahedron jiggles in place. Each nearby enemy takes 5 acid damage. Each creature engulfed by the cube takes a –4 penalty to its saves until the end of its next turn.</p><p><b>2.</b> The cubahedron moves as a quick action. If the cube ends its move engaged with enemies, each of those enemies must roll a save; on a failure, the cubahedron grabs them (but they’re not engulfed).</p><p><b>3.</b> The cubahedron spits an engulfed creature into the air above it and makes a <i>shlup’n’schlorp</i> attack against that creature with a +5 attack bonus. Then the creature is engulfed again.</p><p><b>4.</b> The cubahedron flattens itself slightly and crawls up a wall and possibly across the ceiling. The cube falls at the end of its turn. Each creature engulfed by the cube takes 30 damage, and it makes a <i>gel drop</i> attack against enemies below it.</p><p><b>Gel drop +10 vs. PD (1d3 nearby enemies)</b> — 15 damage, and the cube engulfs the target if it’s smaller than the cube</p><p><b>5.</b> The cubahedron moves one creature engulfed by it to the surface. The target gains a +4 bonus to attempts to escape the cube, but each time the cube is targeted by an attack, the engulfed creature must roll a save; on a failure, it becomes the target of the attack instead.</p><p><b>6.</b> The cubahedron spits out each enemy engulfed by it with great force in different directions; each of those creatures takes 50 damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>200</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Gelatinous Dodecahedron

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Huge</b></p><p><b>7<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Blocker</b></p><p><b>Ooze</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +5</p><p><b>Shlup’n’schlorp +10 vs. PD</b> — 30 acid damage, and the dodecahedron engulfs the target (functions like a grab; see below) if it’s smaller than the dodecahedron<br> <i>Miss:</i> The cube can make a <i>spasms</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: Spasms +10 vs. AC (up to 2 attacks, each against a different nearby enemy)</b> — 15 damage</p><p><i>Engulf and dissolve:</i> Targets engulfed/grabbed by the cube take 30 acid damage at the start of the cube’s turn but are not viable targets for additional attacks by the cube. Multiple targets can be held within the cube simultaneously.<br> Any engulfed creature that is also staggered must begin making last gasp saves or become paralyzed as the cube’s toxins overwhelm it.</p><p><i>Instinctive actions:</i> Gelatinous creatures have no brains, sometimes they just <i>do things</i>. When the escalation die is odd, instead of making an attack or moving, roll a d12 to see what the dodecahedron does. If an option is not available (you roll a 1 but there are no nearby enemies), reroll until you get a valid option.</p><p><b>1.</b> The dodecahedron makes a <i>squash</i> attack against 1d4 nearby enemies as it rolls and shlorps around the area. Any enemies already engulfed by the dodecahedron take 10 thunder damage.</p><p><b>C: Squash +10 vs. PD (1d4 nearby enemies)</b> — 20 damage, and the target is stunned (easy save ends, 6+)</p><p><b>2.</b> The dodecahedron throws out whip-like tendrils and makes a <i>sudden orifice</i> attack against each enemy engaged with it. Then it pulls each nearby enemy next to it and engages that creature.</p><p><b>Sudden orifice +12 vs. PD (each enemy engaged with it)</b> — The dodecahedron engulfs the target if it’s smaller than the dodecahedron</p><p><b>3.</b> Hundreds of finger-size slimes slither out from the interior of the dodecahedron and begin worming their way across the bodies of each of its enemies in the battle. Until the end of the battle, when a non-ooze creature takes any damage besides ongoing acid damage, it also takes 10 acid damage.</p><p><b>4.</b> The dodecahedron bounces and thrums. Each enemy engaged with it or engulfed by it must roll a save; on a failure, that enemy takes 30 thunder damage. On a success, it takes 15 thunder damage and pops free from the dodecahedron.</p><p><b>5.</b> The dodecahedron hunkers down and produces acidic spikes. It gains a +4 bonus to all defenses until the end of the battle, and each enemy who makes a melee attack against it with a non-magical weapon must roll a save; on a failure the weapon dissolves. When a creature’s weapon dissolves, that creature is hampered and weakened (save ends both). Magical weapons lose their bonuses to hit and damage until the end of the battle instead of being dissolved (but the owner is still hampered and weakened). They can be “restored” after the battle by taking a few minutes during a rest to re-attune them.</p><p><b>6.</b> The dodecahedron moves, rolling around the battlefield, then makes a <i>shlup’n’schlorp</i> attack at the end of its movement with a +5 bonus. If the attack misses, instead of making a <i>spasms</i> attack the dodecahedron rolls about the area again and makes a second <i>shlup’n’schlorp</i> attack with a +10 bonus. If the second attack misses, it doesn’t get a <i>spasms</i> attack and the dodecahedron’s turn ends.</p><p><b>7.</b> The dodecahedron makes a <i>spasms</i> attack. If it misses with either attack roll, after the attacks, it can make a <i>stretch and engulf</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><b>C: Stretch and engulf +12 vs. PD (one nearby or far away enemy)</b> — 30 acid damage, and the dodecahedron engulfs the target if it’s smaller than the dodecahedron</p><p><b>8. C: Pseudopod slaps +10 vs. AC (one nearby enemy)</b> — 25 thunder damage<br> <i>Natural odd hit:</i> The target pops free from the dodecahedron and is knocked far away, and the ooze makes the attack again against a different nearby enemy as a free action.<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The dodecahedron engulfs the target if it’s smaller than the dodecahedron.</p><p><b>9.</b> Each enemy engulfed by the dodecahedron takes 40 acid damage, and the dodecahedron heals 40 hp for each enemy it has engulfed.</p><p><b>10.</b> The dodecahedron splits into an octahedron and a tetrahedron, and each one can act this turn (roll a d8 and d4 for the <i>instinctive actions</i> of each one). Divide the dodecahedron’s current hit points into thirds, and give one third to the tetrahedron and two thirds to the octahedron.</p><p><b>11.</b> The dodecahedron splits into three tetrahedrons, and each one can act this turn (roll a d4 for the <i>instinctive actions</i> of each one). Divide the dodecahedron’s current hit points equally between the three new creatures.</p><p><b>12.</b> The dodecahedron splits into two cubahedrons, and each one can act this turn (roll a d6 for the <i>instinctive actions</i> of each one). Divide the dodecahedron’s current hit points equally between the two new creatures.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>550</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Gelatinous Octahedron

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Huge</b></p><p><b>6<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Blocker</b></p><p><b>Ooze</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +5</p><p><b>Shlup’n’schlorp +11 vs. PD</b> — 38 acid damage, and the cube engulfs the target (functions like a grab; see below) if it’s smaller than the cube<br> <i>Miss:</i> The cube can make a <i>spasms</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: Spasms +11 vs. AC (up to 2 attacks, each against a different nearby enemy)</b> — 19 damage</p><p><i>Engulf and dissolve:</i> Targets engulfed/grabbed by the cube take 38 acid damage at the start of the cube’s turn but are not viable targets for additional attacks by the cube. Multiple targets can be held within the cube simultaneously.<br> Any engulfed creature that is also staggered must begin making last gasp saves or become paralyzed as the cube’s toxins overwhelm it.</p><p><i>Instinctive actions:</i> Gelatinous creatures have no brains, sometimes they just <i>do things</i>. When the escalation die is odd, instead of making an attack or moving, roll a d8 to see what the octahedron does. If an option is not viable (you roll a 3 but there are no nearby targets), reroll until you get a valid option.</p><p><b>1. C: Acid splash +11 vs. PD (1d3 nearby or far away enemies in a group)</b> — 8 ongoing acid damage<br> <i>Each failed save:</i> Acid destroys one of the target’s non-magical items. The target takes a cumulative –1 attack penalty until the end of the battle (boots fall apart, shield straps snap, etc.).<br> <i>Miss:</i> 5 ongoing acid damage.</p><p><b>2.</b> The octahedron grows an orifice that gushes out a liquid glue that floods the area. Each enemy engaged with the octahedron is stuck (hard save ends, 16+). Each nearby enemy not engaged with the octahedron is stuck (save ends). Each far away enemy is stuck (easy save ends, 6+). The glue has no effect on creatures who are flying or that have some way of avoiding it.</p><p><b>3.</b> The octahedron squirts a slick slime that targets 1d3 nearby enemies. Until the end of the battle, each target must roll an easy save each time it moves; on a failure, it’s hampered until the end of its next turn.</p><p><b>4.</b> The octahedron makes a <i>fire gout</i> attack as it splashes out a gel that ignites in the air and sticks to skin and clothing.</p><p><b>C: Fire gout +11 vs. PD (1d3 nearby or far away enemies in a group)</b> — 8 ongoing fire damage<br> <i>Each failed save:</i> The ongoing damage for all enemies hit by the attack increases by 1.</p><p><b>5.</b> The octahedron sweats acid. Each enemy engaged with the octahedron must roll a normal save; on a failure, it takes 40 acid damage. On a success it takes 20 acid damage.</p><p><b>6. C: Acid jet +11 vs. PD (one nearby or far away enemy)</b> — 45 acid damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 8 ongoing acid damage.</p><p><b>7. C: Acid geyser +11 vs. PD (1d3 nearby or far away enemies)</b> — 30 acid damage, and the octahedron is propelled uncontrollably about the area, passing next to each of its enemies. Unlike normal, each enemy can make an opportunity attack against the ooze as it moves this way, but the ooze can make a <i>glomp</i> attack against those who do as a free action as it passes. (Tell the PCs that the ooze will get a counter-attack.)</p><p><b>Glomp +9 vs. PD</b> — 10 acid damage, and the cube engulfs the target if it’s smaller than the cube</p><p><b>8.</b> The octahedron splits into two tetrahedrons, and each one can act this turn (roll a d4 for the <i>instinctive actions</i> of each one). Divide the octahedron’s current hit points equally between the two new creatures.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>280</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Gelatinous Tetrahedron

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Huge</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Blocker</b></p><p><b>Ooze</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +3</p><p><b>Shlup’n’schlorp +9 vs. PD</b> — 22 acid damage, and the tetrahedron engulfs the target (functions like a grab; see below) if it’s smaller than the tetrahedron<br> <i>Miss:</i> The tetrahedron can make a <i>spasms</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: Spasms +9 vs. AC (up to 2 attacks, each against a different nearby enemy)</b> — 11 damage</p><p><i>Engulf and dissolve:</i> Targets engulfed/grabbed by the tetrahedron take 22 acid damage at the start of the cube’s turn but are not viable targets for additional attacks by the tetrahedron. Multiple targets can be held within the tetrahedron simultaneously.<br> Any engulfed creature that is also staggered must begin making last gasp saves or become paralyzed as the tetrahedron’s toxins overwhelm it.</p><p><i>Instinctive actions:</i> Gelatinous creatures have no brains, sometimes they just <i>do things</i>. When the escalation die is odd, instead of making an attack or moving, roll a d4 to see what the tetrahedron does. If an option is not viable (you roll a 1 but there is no engaged enemy), reroll until you get a valid option.</p><p><b>1. C: Fling +9 vs. PD (one engaged enemy)</b> — 14 damage, and the target pops free from the ooze and must roll an easy save (6+); on a failure, it loses its next move action</p><p><b>2. C: Fling +9 vs. PD (one nearby enemy not engaged with the ooze)</b> — 28 damage, and the target is flung somewhere nearby and must roll an easy save (6+); on a failure, it loses its next move action</p><p><b>3. C: Fling +9 vs. PD (one far away enemy)</b> — 42 damage, and the target is flung somewhere far away and must roll an easy save (6+); on a failure, it loses its next move action</p><p><b>4.</b> As a standard action the ooze quickly moves around the battlefield, oozing over 1d3 nearby enemies. Those enemies become engaged with the ooze and stuck (save ends).<br> <i>First failed save:</i> The target is engulfed instead of stuck.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>160</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Genie

### Djinn

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>9<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Giant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +15</p><p><b>Greatsword +13 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 40 damage<br> <i>Natural 5, 10, 15, 20:</i> Increase the escalation die by 1 (cumulative), and until the end of the battle, the djinn adds the escalation die to its attacks.</p><p><b>C: Assault of the whirlwind +13 vs. PD (1d4 + 1 nearby creatures, including invisible creatures)</b> — 35 damage, and after the attack the djinn teleports to one of the targets and engages it<br> <i>Natural 5, 10, 15, 20:</i> The target is hampered until the end of its next turn.<br> <i>Miss:</i> 10 damage.<br> <i>Limited use:</i> The djinn can only use this attack while it’s not staggered.</p><p><i>Flight:</i> Genies fly extremely well, but lumber, at best, when walking on the ground.</p><p><i>Grant-a-wish:</i> A PC whose attack drops a djinn to 0 hp gains the equivalent of an extremely favorable roll of 6 with an icon relationship die with an icon of the PC’s choice that the PC already has a positive or conflicted relationship with. Treat this advantage as if it came from a positive relationship. The GM is encouraged to treat this result with the utmost benevolence and compassion.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p>If you want a djinn to be even tougher, add a nastier special depending on which icon or icons the djinn is presently working for. The abilities represent the innate magic of the genie being channeled through the influence of the icon.</p><p>Magic or Religious Icon<br><i>Protection boon:</i> While not staggered, the djinn gains <i>resist spell damage 16+</i> against all spells except those cast by a PC that has at least a one point icon relationship with the Magic or Religious Icons.</p><p>Zealous Icon<br><i>Spiky bits:</i> When an enemy makes a melee attack against the djinn and misses, it takes 2d20 damage.</p><p>Demonic Icon<br><i>Demonic taint:</i> The djinn gains a random demonic feature from the Demonic Abilities table.</p><p>Underground Icon<br><i>Unwelcome resonance:</i> Whenever a nearby enemy attempts to trigger a magic item power, there’s a 50% chance that the power fails. If it does, the item refuses to let its owner use that power until the end of the battle.</p><p>Graceful or Draconic Icon<br><i>Sorcerous reach:</i> The djinn’s <i>assault of the whirlwind</i> attack can also target far away enemies.</p><p>Leader or Undead Icon<br><i>Aura of command:</i> Twice per battle as a free action, the djinn can turn an ally’s normal save into an easy save (6+), or an enemy’s normal save into a hard save (16+).</p><p>Nature or Trickster Icon<br><i>Wind/Shadow form:</i> While not staggered, the djinn has <i>resist melee damage 16+</i>.</p><p>Brute Icon<br><i>Frenzied:</i> The djinn takes a –1 penalty to all defenses. While not staggered, its crit range expands by 3.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>25</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>350</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Efreet

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>10<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Giant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +15<br>Vulnerability: cold (only while staggered)</p><p><b>Blade of the perfect warrior +15 vs. AC (3 attacks)</b> — 35 damage<br> <i>Natural 5, 10, 15, 20:</i> Each nearby enemy takes 20 fire damage.</p><p><b>R: Jet of absolute conflagration +15 vs. PD (one random nearby conscious enemy)</b> — 110 fire damage<br> <i>Natural 5, 10, 15, 20:</i> The target loses all fire resistance until the end of the battle and is hampered (save ends).</p><p><i>Flight:</i> Efreet don’t fly as well or as quickly as djinn, but they are able to get around okay.</p><p><i>Grant-a-wish:</i> A PC whose attack drops an efreet to 0 hp gains the equivalent of an extremely favorable roll of 6 with an icon relationship die with an icon of the PC’s choice that the PC already has a positive or conflicted relationship with. Treat this advantage as if it came from a positive relationship. The GM is encouraged to treat this result with the utmost benevolence and compassion.</p><p><i>Resist fire 18+:</i> When a fire attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 18+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p>If you want an efreet to be even tougher, add a nastier special depending on which icon or icons the efreet is presently working for. The abilities represent the innate magic of the genie being channeled through the influence of the icon.</p><p>Magic or Religious Icon<br><i>Reinforced aura/spirit:</i> The efreet gains a +1 bonus to MD and has no vulnerability to cold while staggered.</p><p>Zealous Icon<br><i>Spiky bits:</i> When an enemy makes a melee attack against the efreet and misses, it takes 2d20 damage.</p><p>Demonic Icon<br><i>Demonic taint:</i> The efreet gains a random demonic feature from the Demonic Ability table.</p><p>Underground or Undead Icon<br><i>Stone slumbers:</i> When the escalation die is 4+ at the start of a round, reset the escalation value by rolling it.</p><p>Graceful or Draconic Icon<br><i>Energy transformation:</i> The efreet can choose to deal lightning damage instead of fire damage with its attacks.</p><p>Leader Icon<br><i>Iconic mark:</i> While not staggered, the efreet gains resist damage 16+ against enemies that have a positive or conflicted relationship with the efreet’s icon.</p><p>Nature or Trickster Icon<br><i>Wind/Shadow form:</i> While not staggered, the efreet gains resist melee damage 16+.</p><p>Brute Icon<br><i>Frenzied:</i> The efreet takes a –1 penalty to all defenses. While not staggered, its crit range expands by 3.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>25</b></p><p><b>24</b></p><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>420</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Ghoul

For nastier specials, instead of a slow, poisonous bite, a more deadly bite can also make things challenging for adventurers. Each time a ghoul bites a character, that PC immediately loses a recovery. If they run out of recoveries before their next full heal-up, that character must start making last gasp saves at the start of each battle. If the character fails their fourth last gasp save this way, they turn into a ghoul.

### Ghast

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +12</p><p><b>Finely honed claws +11 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 8 damage, and the target is vulnerable (save ends)</p><p><b>Paralyzing bite +11 vs. AC (one vulnerable enemy)</b> — 12 damage, and the target is stunned (save ends)</p><p><b>C: Hungry howl +11 vs. MD (each nearby enemy)</b> — The target must choose one: 15 psychic damage; OR 5 psychic damage and the target is vulnerable (save ends)<br> <i>Limited use:</i> 1/battle.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>74</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Ghoul

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +8<br>Vulnerability: holy</p><p><b>Claws and bite +8 vs. AC</b> — 8 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target is vulnerable (<i>attacks vs. it have crit range expanded by 2</i>) to attacks by undead until the end of the ghoul’s next turn.</p><p><i>Pound of flesh:</i> The ghoul’s <i>claws and bite</i> attack deals +4 damage against vulnerable targets.</p><p><i>Infected bite:</i> Any creature that is slain by a ghoul and not consumed will rise as a ghoul the next night.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Paralyzing bite:</i> When the ghoul hits a vulnerable target with a natural even attack roll, the target is also stunned (save ends).</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>12</b></p><p><b>36</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Bergship Raider (Frost)

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>7<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Giant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +10<br>Vulnerability: fire</p><p><b>Whirling ice hook +13 vs. AC</b> — 50 damage, and the target takes a –5 penalty to disengage checks until the end of its next turn<br> <i>Miss:</i> 15 damage to each enemy engaged with the giant.</p><p><b>R: Frost chain +13 vs. AC (one nearby enemy or far away enemy at –2 atk)</b> — 40 damage, and the target is pulled next to the giant, who engages it</p><p><i>Ancient cold:</i> While battling one or more frost giants, there is only a 50% chance that the escalation die increases at the start of the round.</p><p><i>Resist cold 16+:</i> When a cold attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 16+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><i>Winter’s bite:</i> When the escalation die is odd, each enemy engaged with the raider takes 35 cold damage at the start of its turn.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Overbearing:</i> Twice per battle, the raider can make a <i>knockdown</i> attack as a quick action (once per round).</p><p><b>Knockdown +10 vs. PD (one enemy smaller than it)</b> — 20 damage, and the target can’t disengage until the end of its next turn.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>270</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Fire Giant

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>8<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Giant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +12<br>Vulnerability: cold</p><p><b>Flaming greatsword +13 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 35 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The target also takes 10 ongoing fire damage.</p><p><b>R: Flaming black-iron javelin +11 vs. AC</b> — 40 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The target also takes 10 ongoing fire damage.</p><p><i>Fiery escalator:</i> The fire giant adds the escalation die to its attacks against targets taking ongoing fire damage.</p><p><i>Resist fire 16+:</i> When a fire attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 16+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Burning blood:</i> When a fire giant becomes staggered, it deals 10 ongoing fire damage to each enemy engaged with it.</p><p><i>Strength of giants:</i> Twice per battle, the giant can make a <i>slam</i> attack as a quick action (once per round).</p><p><b>Slam +12 vs. PD (one enemy smaller than it)</b> — 10 damage, the target pops free from the giant, and the target loses its next move action</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>25</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>285</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Ice Sorceress (Frost)

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>7<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Caster</b></p><p><b>Giant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +10<br>Vulnerability: fire</p><p><b>Icicle staff +14 vs. AC</b> — 20 damage, 20 cold damage, and the sorceress can make an <i>icy delusions</i> attack against the target as a free action</p><p><b>R: Winter wind +14 vs. PD</b> — 55 cold damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The sorceress can make an <i>icy delusions</i> attack against the target as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: Icy delusions +14 vs. MD (one enemy)</b> — At the start of each round, the target loses 2d6 points from their initiative count as they slowly freeze from the inside out (save ends)<br> <i>Frozen flesh:</i> When a creature is reduced to 0 initiative or lower from <i>icy delusions</i>, it becomes delusional and frozen and must choose one condition that will affect it: confused (hard save ends, 16+); OR stunned (save ends). After saving, the creature rerolls its initiative.</p><p><i>Ice summoner:</i> Once per round as a free action, the giant can make an <i>ice wall</i> attack to conjure forth a wall of ice that stops one enemy’s movement or ranged attack. The giant can’t use this ability to target creatures making fire attacks or wielding weapons that deal fire damage.</p><p><b>C: Ice wall +14 vs. PD (one moving enemy or ranged attacker)</b> — The target stops its movement or loses its ranged attack that turn, and the wall of ice remains until the end of the battle (GM’s choice on its size, but it shouldn’t be too large or thick; normal DC to break through it)</p><p><i>Ancient cold:</i> While battling one or more frost giants, there is only a 50% chance that the escalation die increases at the start of the round.</p><p><i>Resist cold 16+:</i> When a cold attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 16+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Ice armor:</i> The ice sorceress has <i>resist damage 16+</i> unless the attack deals fire damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>190</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Ice Zombie

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>6<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +5<br>Vulnerability: fire, holy</p><p><b>Chill claws +11 vs. AC</b> — 12 cold damage</p><p><b>Icy breath of the grave +11 vs. PD</b> — 9 cold damage, and the target is vulnerable to cold attacks (save ends)</p><p><i>Resist cold 18+:</i> When a cold attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 18+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><i>Fiery decapitation:</i> Ice zombies have frozen, iron-hard flesh that makes them tougher than normal zombies—critical hits that deal fire damage deal triple damage to ice zombies; other critical hits just deal double damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>20</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Jotun Auroch

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Huge</b></p><p><b>6<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +7</p><p><b>Trampling hooves +8 vs. PD</b> — 6 damage<br> <i>Natural 1–5:</i> The jotun auroch can make a <i>fiery or frosty breath</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: Fiery or Frosty breath +10 vs. PD (1d4 nearby enemies)</b> — 5 fire or cold damage, depending on what the jotun auroch has been eating lately</p><p><i>Resist cold and fire 18+:</i> When a cold or fire attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 18+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>70</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Stone Giant

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>8<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Troop</b></p><p><b>Giant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +11</p><p><b>Stone club +13 vs. AC</b> — 50 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The stone giant can also make a <i>stomp</i> attack against a single target as a free action.</p><p><b>Stomp +13 vs. PD (each smaller enemy engaged with the giant)</b> — 30 damage, and the target is dazed (save ends)</p><p><b>R: Thrown boulder +11 vs. PD (one nearby or far away enemy)</b> — 40 damage<br> <i>Natural even miss:</i> 20 damage.</p><p><i>Built of stone:</i> The stone giant has <i>resist weapons 16+</i>.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>24</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>270</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Storm Giant

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Huge</b></p><p><b>10<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Archer</b></p><p><b>Giant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +16</p><p><b>Truly enormous greatsword +15 vs. AC</b> — 120 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The giant can make a <i>lightning bolt</i> attack against a random nearby enemy as a free action.<br> <i>Miss:</i> 40 damage OR the giant can make a <i>release the thunder</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><b>R: Giant longbow +14 vs. AC (2 attacks vs. nearby or far away enemies)</b> — 60 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The giant can make a <i>lightning bolt</i> attack against a random enemy that is nearby the target of the <i>longbow</i> attack.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: Lightning bolt +15 vs. PD (one random nearby enemy)</b> — 2d6 × 10 lightning damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> Half damage.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: Release the thunder +15 vs. PD (all nearby creatures)</b> — 1d10 thunder damage per <i>building thunder</i> point (see below)<br> <i>Miss:</i> Half damage.</p><p><i>Building thunder:</i> Keep count of the number of times the storm giant uses its <i>lightning bolt</i> attack during the battle. Add that number to the escalation die to get the current building thunder value.</p><p><i>Skystep:</i> A storm giant can use its standard action to walk or run through the air, using move actions to continue. If the storm giant makes a standard action attack, it settles back to the ground below it without falling.</p><p><i>Storm born:</i> The storm giant has <i>resist thunder 16+</i> and <i>resist lightning 16+</i>.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>26</b></p><p><b>24</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>650</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Winter Beast

## Gnoll

Nastier Specials for all gnolls

_Blood fury:_ +1d10 melee damage if the gnoll or its target is staggered.

### Gnoll Fiendfletch

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>7<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Archer</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +11</p><p><b>Infernal mace +12 vs. AC</b> — 18 damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The fiendfletch can make a disengage check as a free action this turn after the attack.</p><p><b>R: Hellbent bow +13 vs. AC</b> — 30 damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The target is dazed until the end of its next turn as it suffers debilitating pain from a hellish arrow.</p><p><i>Close-quarters archery:</i> While making a ranged attack, the fiendfletch gains a +4 bonus to AC against opportunity attacks.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Duck and cover:</i> While the fiendfletch has at least one blocker, troop, or wrecker ally (like a shredder) between it and an enemy, it gains a +4 bonus to all defenses against ranged and close-quarters attacks from that enemy.</p><p><i>Living arrows:</i> When the fiendfletch rolls a natural 16+ with a <i>hellbent bow</i> attack and hits, the target is weakened (save ends) instead of dazed.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>75</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

On a 11+, the gnoll ranger can make a <i>longbow</i> attack against that enemy as a free action just before being engaged.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Hates everyone:</i> The crit range of attacks by gnoll rangers expands by 2 against humanoids.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>46</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>
