## Golem

### Bronze Golem

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>7<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Blocker</b></p><p><b>Construct</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +11</p><p><b>Gong-like fists of bronze +12 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 20 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit against a target in heavy armor:</i> The target is dazed (save ends).<br> <i>Natural odd hit against a target in light armor or no armor:</i> The target takes 10 extra damage.<br> <i>Miss:</i> 4d6 damage.</p><p><i>Golem immunity:</i> Non-organic golems are immune to effects. They can’t be dazed, weakened, confused, made vulnerable, or touched by ongoing damage. You can damage a golem, but that’s about it.</p><p><i>Hidden flaw:</i> An enemy who hits the bronze golem with a natural 18+ attack roll can roll a DC 25 skill check using Intelligence or Wisdom to notice the bronze golem’s hidden flaw! On a success, until the end of the battle, the golem loses its damage resistance and becomes vulnerable to all attacks (against each enemy informed of the flaw).</p><p><i>Resist damage 18+:</i> When an attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 18+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Percussion resonance:</i> When the escalation die reaches 3+, the bronze golem gains a bonus to its first <i>gong-like fists of bronze</i> attack roll each turn equal to the number of attacks made against it so far that turn. (Each turn is separate, not cumulative.)</p><p><i>Spiky:</i> When an enemy engaged with the bronze golem misses it with a melee attack, that enemy takes 2d12 damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>190</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Clay Golem

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>6<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Construct</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +6</p><p><b>Bare brutal hands +10 vs. AC</b> — 36 damage<br> <i>Cursed wound:</i> A non-dwarf creature damaged by a clay golem can’t be healed to above half its maximum hit points until after the battle.</p><p><i>Golem immunity:</i> Non-organic golems are immune to effects. They can’t be dazed, weakened, confused, made vulnerable, or touched by ongoing damage. You can damage a golem, but that’s about it.</p><p><i>Ignore attacks 11+:</i> When an attack hits this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 11+ on the attack roll or it misses instead. That’s <i>all</i> attacks.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>120</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Flesh Golem

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Blocker</b></p><p><b>Construct</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +5</p><p><b>Sweeping fists +9 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 15 damage</p><p><b>Maddened battlefield repairs +11 vs. AC (one staggered living enemy)</b> — 20 damage, and the flesh golem heals 2d10 hit points<br> <i>Miss:</i> 10 damage, and the flesh golem heals 1d10 hit points.<br> <i>Limited use:</i> The flesh golem can only use this attack while it’s staggered.</p><p><i>Energy magnet:</i> Whenever a spell that causes cold, fire, force, lightning, or negative energy damage targets one of the flesh golem’s nearby allies, the flesh golem has a 50% chance of becoming the main target instead. Therefore, spells that affect groups would spread out from the flesh golem.</p><p><i>Weakness of the flesh:</i> Unlike other golems, flesh golems are not immune to effects.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>100</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Iron Golem

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>10<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Construct</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +13</p><p><b>Fists of iron +17 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 50 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 5d10 damage.</p><p><i>Golem immunity:</i> Non-organic golems are immune to effects. They can’t be dazed, weakened, confused, made vulnerable, or touched by ongoing damage. You can damage a golem, but that’s about it.</p><p><i>Rampage:</i> At the start of each of the iron golem’s turns, roll a d6. If the roll is equal to or less than the escalation die, the iron golem goes on a rampage that turn. Instead of its two normal <i>fists of iron</i> attacks, it can make three attacks with <i>fists of iron</i>, each against a different random nearby creature, enemy or ally. It can move after each such attack as a free action, if necessary, taking only half damage from opportunity attacks during the rampage.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Poison gas:</i> The first time the iron golem is staggered, poison gas leaks from it into the area. It can make a <i>poison gas cloud</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: Poison gas cloud +15 vs. PD (all nearby creatures)</b> — 25 ongoing poison damage</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>28</b></p><p><b>24</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>360</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Marble Golem

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>9<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Troop</b></p><p><b>Construct</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +10</p><p><b>Enormous maul +15 vs. AC</b> — 60 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The golem can make a <i>backswing</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>Backswing +14 vs. PD</b> — 40 damage</p><p><i>Golem immunity:</i> Non-organic golems are immune to effects. They can’t be dazed, weakened, confused, made vulnerable, or touched by ongoing damage. You can damage a golem, but that’s about it.</p><p><span>Special Virtues</span></p><p>Each marble golem is infused with <i>two</i> virtues—magical properties that relate to the emotion or feeling incorporated into the sculpture as its dominant theme. Choose two virtues from the list below, or for a unique marble golem, invent your own.</p><p><i>Awe (fear effect):</i> While nearby the golem, enemies with 40 hp or fewer are dazed (–4 attack) and do not add the escalation die to their attacks.</p><p><i>Beauty:</i> The first time each enemy attacks the marble golem this battle, it must roll a normal save; on a failure, the attack takes a –6 penalty.</p><p><i>Courage:</i> While staggered, the marble golem adds the escalation die to its attack rolls.</p><p><i>Endurance:</i> When the marble golem rolls a natural 1–5 with an attack roll, it heals 1d10 hit points per point on the escalation die. (It was checking for damage and got distracted.)</p><p><i>Hatred:</i> When an enemy is staggered by the marble golem’s attack, that enemy takes 4d10 extra damage.</p><p><i>Patience:</i> Each turn, the marble golem can use one standard action to gain a +2 bonus to all defenses until the start of its next turn. If it does, it gains an extra standard action during its next turn.</p><p><i>Protection:</i> When the marble golem rolls a natural 16+ with an attack, decrease the escalation die by 1.</p><p><i>Strength:</i> The marble golem’s melee attacks now deal half damage on a miss.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>More virtues:</i> Statues that capture even more themes make stronger marble golems. Add one or two more virtues to the golem.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>25</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>340</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Stone Golem

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>8<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Blocker</b></p><p><b>Construct</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +11</p><p><b>Massive stone fists +12 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 35 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 15 damage.</p><p><b>Finishing smash +14 vs. AC (one staggered enemy)</b> — 80 damage, and the golem pops the target off it and moves it a short distance away from the golem<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> 20 damage, and the target is hampered (save ends).<br> <i>Natural odd hit or miss:</i> 20 damage, and the target is dazed (save ends).</p><p><i>Golem immunity:</i> Non-organic golems are immune to effects. They can’t be dazed, weakened, confused, made vulnerable, or touched by ongoing damage. You can damage a golem, but that’s about it.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Former idol:</i> Evoke the powers of an ancient culture’s strange rites by giving the stone golem any weird power you wish. If you’re stuck for inspiration, consider starting with random abilities from the demons that aren’t related to energy or the <i>cone of cold</i> from the ogre mage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>25</b></p><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>280</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Hag

Hags get two of the following abilities, and a single death curse.

Abilities: Choose TWO

**Adept Illusionist:** The hag gains a +5 bonus to initiative checks due to being not quite where she seems.  
 _Hag ability:_ As a distraction, the hag creates an illusion of her doing one thing, when she is in fact setting a trap. The hag throws out a bear-trap or other impediment and one nearby enemy becomes stuck (save ends). While stuck this way, the target takes 6 damage at the start of each of its turns.

**Another skin:** On the hag’s first round of combat each battle, she gains a +2 attack bonus due to her victims being shocked as she bursts out of her false outer skin.  
 _Hag ability:_ The hag coughs up a glob of liquid pseudo-flesh that globs onto a nearby enemy (no attack roll). The glob solidifies causing an effect of the hag’s choice: the target is stuck (save ends); OR the target is unable to cast spells during its next turn (the pseudo-flesh covers their mouth and face).

**Blood pact:** Each creature allied to the hag through a pact gains a +2 bonus with their first attack each battle if the hag is present.  
 _Hag ability:_ The hag spits blood in the face of the target and makes a command. The target must roll an immediate save; on a failure, as a free action it makes basic attack against an ally or against itself (target’s choice).

**Breath stealing:** The hag starts combat with 10 temporary hit points.  
 _Hag ability:_ The hag steals a recovery from the target and heals 20 hp.

**Death shriek:** When a melee attack hits the hag, she lets out a shriek as a free action and the attacker takes 2d4 thunder damage.  
 _Hag ability:_ The hag begins to shriek, and each enemy in the battle takes a –4 attack penalty with spells until the start of her next turn.

**Dusk walk:** Once per day the hag can implant a suggestion in the mind of a target sleeping within a day’s travel of her. The hag rolls an attack: **+10 vs. MD**; on a hit, she implants a suggestion in the target that they must obey when a condition she chooses is met. Suggested actions can’t cause direct harm (the target can’t be forced to fight another or harm themselves), can be no longer than 12 words, and affects the target for a week or until triggered. GM keeps the roll hidden.  
 _Hag ability:_ The hag becomes immaterial, pops free from all enemies engaged with her, and enters the land of dreams, re-appearing next to any nearby conscious creature (or a nearby or far away creature that is unconscious). The hag then makes the following attack: **C: +10 vs. MD (each nearby unconscious enemy)** — The hag implants a suggestion in the target that they must obey when they become conscious (usually “When you awake, flee this fight and discard your equipment.”) Suggested actions can’t cause direct harm. The round after the target acts on the implanted suggestion it can start rolling normal saves to throw off the effect.

**Fateful visions:** The hag uses a +2 magical weapon traded to her for her services (she gains a +2 bonus to attack and damage with melee attacks).  
 _Hag ability:_ The hag has seen this fight in a vision. Her crit range expands by 2 until the end of the battle. Each increase is cumulative.

**Foul-touched:** When an enemy is battling the hag, at the start of each of its turns, it takes 2d6 psychic damage from the horror of the hag’s visage unless it takes precautions to avoid directly glancing at her terrible face (mirror, blindfold, etc., which might cause attack penalties).  
 _Hag ability:_ The hag chooses a nearby enemy and glares at it. That target must roll an immediate save; on a failure, the target is stricken blind by her ugliness. While blinded this way, the target is hampered, weakened, and can’t make ranged attacks. The target can end the effect by splashing liquid into their eyes or using a similar act to clear the ugly out as a standard action.

**Song of dreams:** Enemies take a –4 penalty to their initiative rolls in battles with the hag.  
 _Hag ability:_ The hag begins to sing and the two enemies closest to her (even if far away) must roll an immediate save; on a failure, the target is dazed (save ends). If the dazed target fails its first save, instead it’s weakened (save ends). If the weakened target fails its second save, instead it’s helpless (save ends).

**Thief of mist:** The hag ignores opportunity attacks and can’t be intercepted while moving.  
 _Hag ability:_ The hag becomes a mist until the start of her next turn. While a mist, only spells cast with a +3 implement and attacks using a +3 magical weapon can harm her. (Some special story item might also allow attacks to hit if no PC has a +3 item.)

**Twist the path:** Once per day the hag can enspell an area to attract visitors, causing those traveling nearby to get lost and wander to that location. Alternately, the hag can cause the location to repel visitors. Finding the correct path to that location requires a DC 20 check if it is a familiar place, a DC 25 check if the travelers only have a map or guide, or a DC 30 check if the travelers are unfamiliar with the area.  
 _Hag ability:_ The target is also confused (easy save ends, 6+).

**Weakening touch:** Each enemy fighting the hag must roll a normal save at the start of the battle; on a failure, that creature starts the battle weakened (easy save ends, 6+).  
 _Hag ability:_ The target is dazed (save ends). If the dazed target fails its first save, instead it’s weakened (save ends). When the target saves against this effect, it takes a –2 attack penalty until the end of its next turn.

**Winter breath:** The hag’s attacks deal cold damage.  
 _Hag ability:_ The target takes 6 ongoing cold damage.

Death Curses: Create ONE

When a hag dies she curses the one who killed her. The only known way to remove the curse is to seek the aid of another hag, though there may be some ways to end such a curse that are not readily known.

Create one curse per hag. A good curse makes life horribly weird for a character, but isn’t something that debilitates them. Avoid ones that blind, deafen, cripple, or mute characters. Odd habits, ugly features, unusual smells, strange and disgusting diets — all these are good. They should make the character and the story more interesting.

### Hag

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>6<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +10</p><p><b>Iron claws +10 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 9 damage<br> <i>Natural 14+:</i> The hag triggers one <i>hag ability</i> as a free action.<br> <i>Natural 18+:</i> The hag triggers two <i>hag abilities</i> as a free action (can’t be the same ability twice).</p><p><b>R: Evil eye +10 vs. MD</b> — Ongoing 12 damage (hard save ends, 16+)<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The attack roll also targets a second different enemy of the hag’s choice (but not a third with another 16+).<br> <i>Natural 18+:</i> As above, and the attack roll also targets a third different enemy of the hag’s choice (but not a fourth with another 18+).</p><p><i>Death curse:</i> Each hag can lay a curse upon the one who ends its horrible life. After dropping to 0 hit points, a hag always lingers long enough to pronounce the words of the curse. (See Death Curses.)</p><p><i>Delusionist:</i> All hags have the ability to twist the perceptions of others. If the hag has a short time to prepare, it can hide a small hut, disguise a volunteer or captive as a monster, disguise itself as a harmless peasant woman, etc. A DC 30 skill check is required to overcome the delusion and see the truth of it (if a player gives a reason for not trusting what their character sees; perhaps add subtle clues toward that end). The magic fades as soon as the hag enters combat.</p><p><i>Fear:</i> While engaged with this creature, enemies with 30 hp or fewer are dazed (–4 attack) and do not add the escalation die to their attacks.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>108</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Half-Orc

Nastier Special for all half-orcs

_Lethal swing:_ Once per battle, a half-orc can reroll a melee attack and use the result it prefers.

### Half-Orc Commander

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>8<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Leader</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +13</p><p><b>Jagged longsword +15 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 15 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> One nearby lower-level mook makes an attack as a free action.</p><p><b>R: Thrown javelin +13 vs. AC</b> — 20 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The half-orc commander gains 20 temporary hit points.</p><p><i>Orcish command:</i> When a nearby ally of the half-orc commander scores a critical hit, that ally can roll a save against a save ends effect as a free action.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>150</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Half-Orc Legionnaire

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Troop</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +8</p><p><b>Longsword +10 vs. AC</b> — 12 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The half-orc legionnaire gains a +2 bonus to all defenses until the start of its next turn.<br> <i>Natural odd hit:</i> The target takes +1d6 damage.<br> <i>Natural even miss:</i> 4 damage.<br> <i>Natural odd miss:</i> If the legionnaire’s next melee attack is a natural even hit, it becomes a critical hit instead!</p><p><b>R: Javelin +10 vs. AC</b> — 10 damage</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>56</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Half-Orc Tribal Champion

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9</p><p><b>Great axe +9 vs. AC</b> — 18 damage<br> <i>Natural odd miss:</i> The tribal champion heals 5 hp.<br> <i>Natural even miss:</i> 10 damage.</p><p><b>R: Longbow +8 vs. AC</b> — 12 damage</p><p><i>Tribal rage:</i> When the escalation die is even, a tribal champion can roll two d20 for each melee attack roll it makes and use the result it prefers. If both dice are 11+, the melee attack is a critical hit.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>80</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Harpy

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +7</p><p><b>Talons +6 vs. AC</b> — 10 damage<br> <i>Cull:</i> The harpy gains a +5 bonus to attack and damage with this attack against any enemy suffering from any <i>fiendish song</i> effect.</p><p><b>C: Fiendish song +10 vs. MD (1d3 nearby enemies)</b> — 5 psychic damage<br> <i>Natural 16–17:</i> The target is hampered (easy save ends, 6+).<br> <i>Natural 18–19:</i>The target is weakened instead of hampered (easy save ends, 6+).<br> <i>Natural 20:</i> The target is confused instead of weakened (easy save ends, 6+).</p><p><i>Flight:</i> As the standard monster ability.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>44</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Haunted Skull

### Black Skull

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>8<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Caster</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +13</p><p><b>R: Telekinetic grasp +15 vs. PD (1d3 nearby enemies)</b> — 28 force damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target is stuck (save ends).</p><p><i>Telekinetic crush:</i> When the escalation die is even, one enemy of the skull’s choice that is stuck from its <i>telekinetic grasp</i> takes 18 force damage at the start of the skull’s turn. When the escalation die is odd, one such stuck enemy of its choice is hampered (save ends).</p><p><i>Limited flight:</i> The haunted skull glides and hovers, always within seven or eight feet of the ground. If the skull is incognito, its empty clothing moves around beneath it, held in the shape of a person by telekinesis and it stays closer to the ground to appear normal.</p><p><i>Lost opportunity:</i> This creature can’t make opportunity attacks.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>110</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Flaming Skull

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Caster</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +10<br>Vulnerability: holy OR negative energy, depending on the skull</p><p><b>R: Burning gaze +12 vs. PD (1d3 nearby enemies or one far away enemy)</b> — 10 fire damage<br> <i>First natural even hit each battle:</i> The target is confused (easy save ends, 6+).</p><p><b>C: Smoldering flames +11 vs. PD (one nearby enemy)</b> — 14 fire damage, and each time the target fails a save this battle, it bursts into flames and takes 5 ongoing fire damage</p><p><i>Limited flight:</i> The haunted skull can glide and hover, always within seven or eight feet of the ground.</p><p><i>Lost opportunity:</i> This creature can’t make opportunity attacks.</p><p><i>Resist fire 16+:</i> When a fire attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 16+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>12</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>54</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Jest Bones

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +8</p><p><b>C: Puns +11 vs. PD (1d4 nearby enemies)</b> — 5 psychic damage, plus 1d6 ongoing psychic damage if the GM makes a horrible pun while rolling the attacks<br> <i>Bad puns:</i> Creatures that can’t hear or that have attempted to reduce their hearing are only affected by a jest bones’ <i>puns </i>attack if the natural roll is odd.</p><p><i>Limited flight:</i> The haunted skull can glide and hover, always within seven or eight feet of the ground. It also performs barrel rolls.</p><p><i>Lost opportunity:</i> This creature can’t make opportunity attacks.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>11</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>41</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Screaming Skull

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Troop</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +7</p><p><b>C: Treacherous scream +11 vs. MD (up to 2 nearby or far away enemies)</b> — 6 psychic damage, and the target takes 2d6 psychic damage the first time it succeeds at a save before the end of its next turn.</p><p><i>Limited flight:</i> The haunted skull can glide and hover, always within seven or eight feet of the ground.</p><p><i>Lost opportunity:</i> This creature can’t make opportunity attacks.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>11</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>45</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Skull of the Beast

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>9<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +10</p><p><b>Huge club +17 vs. AC</b> — 50 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 18 thunder damage to 1d3 nearby enemies (the beast screams and bellows in disappointment).</p><p><b>C: Baleful gaze +15 vs. PD (1d3 nearby enemies)</b> — 25 negative energy damage<br> <i>Natural odd hit:</i> The target is stuck (save ends) from looking into the void within it.<br> <i>Limited use:</i> 1/battle.</p><p><i>Fear:</i> While engaged with this creature, enemies that have 60 hp or fewer are dazed (–4 attack) and do not add the escalation die to their attacks.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>400</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Slime-Skull

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +5</p><p><b>Slam +10 vs. AC</b> — 7 damage</p><p><b>C: Grasping slime tendrils +10 vs. PD (one nearby enemy)</b> — 7 acid damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The target takes 3 extra acid damage and is stuck (hard save ends, 16+).</p><p><i>Acidic:</i> When a creature is engaged with the slime-skull or stuck from its <i>grasping slime tendrils</i> attack at the start of its turn, it takes 3 acid damage.</p><p><i>Slimy blastback:</i> When an enemy engaged with the slime-skull hits it with a melee attack, the slime-skull fires a blast of acidic slime back at that creature, which takes 1d4 acid damage.</p><p><i>Slow:</i> This creature is slow. It only moves when the escalation die is odd or 6+.</p><p><i>Wall-crawler:</i> A slime-skull can climb on ceilings and walls as easily as it moves on the ground.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Breeder:</i> If the slime-skull kills a creature, it takes that creature’s head as a standard action and attempts to escape (it can squeeze through gaps as small as the skull). The slain creature can’t be resurrected until its skull is recovered because its spirit is now trapped within the skull. If the PCs don’t track down the slime-skull before their next full heal-up (or within a day), the stolen skull will transform into another slime-skull. Attempts to resurrect the creature become much more difficult, perhaps even impossible, at that point.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>10</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>36</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Watch Skull

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>1<sup>st</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Troop</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9</p><p><b>C: Screech +8 vs. MD (1d3 random nearby creatures)</b> — 4 psychic damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The target is stuck (save ends).<br> <i>Natural roll is equal to or lower than the escalation die:</i> 1d3 nearby enemies hear the alarm and join the battle. The creatures attracted by the constant screeching are (usually) level 1 mooks of a type that would be appropriate for the skull’s location.</p><p><i>Immobile:</i> The skull can’t hop, jump, roll, or fly. It can’t even move its jaw.</p><p><i>Lost opportunity:</i> This creature can’t make opportunity attacks.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Allies:</i> Creatures that have been mystically “keyed” to the skull aren’t affected by its <i>screech</i> attack.</p><p><i>Gem eyes:</i> The skull can sense the unseen and things from beyond the world. A wizard using a <i>blur</i> spell, a rogue shadow walking, and other similar abilities offer no protection from the skull and its <i>screech</i> attack. (If the PCs come up with a plausible tactic to bypass the skull, give the skull a normal save to detect them.)</p><p><i>Move-triggered:</i> When an enemy near the skull uses a move action to move, the skull can make a <i>screech</i> attack against that creature as a free action that interrupts the move. The skull can use this ability twice per round. Shadow walking, teleporting, and other non-standard modes of movement will trigger the <i>screech</i> attack.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>11</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>20</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Hellbugs

### Boombug

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>2<sup>nd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Troop</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +5</p><p><b>Gnawing teeth +6 vs. AC</b> — 5 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 2 damage.</p><p><i>Puff go boom:</i> When an enemy’s attack hits the boombug and leaves it staggered with an odd number of hit points, it explodes and dies. (Even hit points does nothing.) When it explodes, each nearby creature not engaged with it takes 1d4 thunder damage, and it makes the following attack against each creature engaged with it.</p><p><b>C: Thunderous explosion +9 vs. PD</b> — 12 thunder damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 5 thunder damage.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Latches on:</i> When the boombug hits with <i>gnawing teeth</i>, the target takes a –5 penalty to disengage checks until it’s no longer engaged with the boombug.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>11</b></p><p><b>36</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Hellwasp

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>2<sup>nd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +8</p><p><b>Necrotizing stinger +6 vs. PD</b> — 5 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> 5 ongoing acid damage (easy save ends, 6+), and the hellwasp can pop free from the target.</p><p><i>Virulent injection:</i> When a creature fails a save against the hellwasp’s ongoing acid damage, it gains a random condition until it saves against that damage. Have the player roll a d4 to determine the condition: 1. confused; 2. weakened; 3. dazed; 4. vulnerable.</p><p><i>Flight:</i> Hellwasps are adroit fliers that can hover and even fly backward.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Lethal injection:</i> The save versus the stinger’s ongoing acid damage is a normal save (11+) instead of an easy save.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>12</b></p><p><b>28</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Hook Scuttler

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>2<sup>nd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Blocker</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +5</p><p><b>Claws and mandibles +7 vs. AC</b> — 8 damage</p><p><i>Spiky bits:</i> When a hook scuttler moves to engage an enemy it wasn’t engaged with at the start of its turn, that enemy takes 1d6 damage. When an enemy tries to disengage from the hook scuttler and fails, it takes 1d6 damage.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Corpse eater:</i> When a nearby enemy drops to 0 hit points or below in the battle, the hook scuttler will ignore other enemies and move to attack that unconscious enemy until that enemy is dead.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>30</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Swarming Maw

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>2<sup>nd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +6</p><p><b>Serrated maw +8 vs. AC</b> — 6 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The swarming maw can teleport to engage a nearby enemy it can see that is already engaged by at least one other hellbug.<br> <i>Miss:</i> The first time each battle the serrated maw misses, the target takes 1d4 damage for each hellbug engaged with it.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Ongoing swarm:</i> The serrated maw also deals miss damage the second time it misses with a <i>serrated maw</i> attack each battle.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>38</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Hellhound

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +5</p><p><b>Savage bite +9 vs. AC</b> — 7 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The hellhound can make a <i>fiery breath</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: Fiery breath +9 vs. PD (1d3 nearby enemies in a group)</b> — 10 fire damage</p><p><i>Resist fire 16+:</i> When a fire attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 16+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Fiery aura:</i> Each creature engaged with a hellhound at the start of its turn takes 2d6 fire damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>11</b></p><p><b>58</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Human

### Blue Sorcerer

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Caster</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9</p><p><b>Nasty dagger or short spear +8 vs. AC</b> — 6 damage</p><p><span>Minor Spell</span></p><p><b>R: Lightning fork +8 vs. PD</b> — 6 lightning damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The sorcerer can target a different nearby enemy with the attack.</p><p><span>Major Spells</span></p><p><b>C: Breath of the Blue +8 vs. PD (one nearby enemy)</b> — 10 lightning damage, and at the start of the target’s next turn, 1d6 nearby allies of the target take 4 lightning damage</p><p><b>C: Chaos orb +8 vs. MD (1d3 nearby enemies)</b> — 8 lightning damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The sorcerer gains one use of the target’s racial power, if any. It must use that power by the end of the battle or lose it, and it can’t use the power this turn.</p><p><i>Power-monger:</i> When the blue sorcerer starts its turn and it didn’t <i>gather power</i> the previous turn, choose whether it will gather power or cast a spell this turn. When it chooses to cast a spell, roll a d20 to see if it uses a minor spell or a major spell: <b>1–10:</b> minor spell; <b>11–20:</b> major spell.</p><p><i>Gather power:</i> Like a PC sorcerer, a blue sorcerer can use its standard action to gather power in order to cast a double-strength and double-damage spell with its next standard action. When it gathers power, the sorcerer rolls a d6 and gains one of the following chaotic benefits.</p><p><b>1–2:</b> The sorcerer gains a +1 bonus to AC until the start of its next turn.</p><p><b>3–4:</b> One nearby enemy of the sorcerer’s choice takes damage equal to sorcerer’s level (3).</p><p><b>5–6:</b> Each nearby enemy engaged with the sorcerer’s allies takes damage equal to sorcerer’s level (3); OR grant one nearby dragon with <i>intermittent breath</i> an additional use of its breath weapon this battle.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Escalating caster:</i> Add the escalation die to the sorcerer’s <i>power-monger</i> rolls and attack rolls.</p><p><i>Sorcerous evasion (kobold sorcerers only):</i> Once per battle when an attack misses the sorcerer, the attacker takes the miss damage from that attack, if any, and the sorcerer takes no damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>48</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Demon-Touched Human Ranger

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Archer</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +10</p><p><b>M or R: Demon bow +10 vs. AC</b> — 15 damage, and the target is dazed (–4 attack) until it pulls the arrow out using a quick action, which deals 10 ongoing damage<br> <i>Natural odd hit or miss:</i> The demon bow eats at the ranger’s arm and the ranger takes 1d6 damage.</p><p><i>Bow teeth:</i> Whenever an attacker hits the ranger with a melee attack, that creature takes 1d6 damage as the bow chews on it.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>80</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Human Thug

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>1<sup>st</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Troop</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +3</p><p><b>Heavy mace +5 vs. AC</b> — 4 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The thug deals +6 damage with its <i>next</i> attack this battle.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>12</b></p><p><b>27</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Hungry Star

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Aberration</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +8</p><p><b>Ripping tentacles +8 vs. AC</b> — 10 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> If the target is taking ongoing psychic damage, the attack deals +2d6 damage.</p><p><i>[Group ability]</i> <b>R: Warp-pulse +8 vs. PD (1d3 enemies in a group)</b> — 5 ongoing psychic damage<br> <i>Natural 16–18:</i> While the target is taking the ongoing psychic damage, it is dazed (–4 attacks).<br> <i>Natural 19–20:</i> While the target is taking the ongoing psychic damage, it is confused instead of dazed.</p><p><i>Group ability:</i> For every two hungry stars in the battle (round up), one of them can use <i>warp-pulse</i> once during the battle.</p><p><i>Limited flight:</i> Hungry stars flap and glide and hover, always within seven or eight feet of the ground.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>12</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>54</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Hydra

### Five-Headed Hydra

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Huge</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9</p><p><b>Gnashing teeth +10 vs. AC (5 attacks)</b> — 10 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The hydra’s next <i>gnashing teeth</i> attack, if it has an attack left this turn, can be against any nearby enemy instead of against a creature engaged with it.<br> <i>Miss:</i> 5 damage.</p><p><i>Too tough to trick:</i> Whenever the hydra would suffer any of the following conditions, it ignores the condition and takes 5 damage instead: Confused, dazed, hampered, stunned, or weakened.</p><p><i>Roiling swirl:</i> If the hydra has at least two <i>gnashing teeth</i> attacks left during a turn, it can expend one of those attacks to move to engage a nearby enemy as a free action (but it will take opportunity attacks for doing so).</p><p><i>Sprout sixth head:</i> The first time the hydra is staggered, as a free action it gains 40 hit points and a sixth <i>gnashing teeth</i> attack, and is considered undamaged at its new hit point total. Using the hydra’s current hit points as a new baseline, the hydra will be staggered again when it drops below 50% of that total.</p><p><i>Sprout seventh head:</i> The second time the hydra is staggered, as a free action it gains 40 hit points and a seventh <i>gnashing teeth</i> attack, etc. Use a new hit point baseline as before, but there is no eighth head waiting to sprout.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Sprout eighth head:</i> You know the drill.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>150</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Seven-Headed Hydra

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Huge</b></p><p><b>7<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +11</p><p><b>Gnashing teeth +12 vs. AC (7 attacks)</b> — 12 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The hydra’s next <i>gnashing teeth</i> attack, if it has an attack left this turn, can be against any nearby enemy instead of against a creature engaged with it.<br> <i>Miss:</i> 7 damage.</p><p><i>Let’s not waste space:</i> The seven-headed hydra has all the same abilities as the five-headed hydra, except that the heads that get sprouted are the 8<sup>th</sup> and 9<sup>th</sup> and those heads/attacks come with 50 new hit points apiece.</p><p>And it has one additional ability…</p><p><i>Resist opportunity attacks 16+:</i> When an opportunity attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 16+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Pyrohydra:</i> When the hydra gets a natural even attack roll with a <i>gnashing teeth</i> attack, its next attack that turn (if it has one) is a <i>flame breath</i> attack instead. Note that <i>flame breath</i> attacks don’t lead to other flaming breaths; the hydra has to return to making a <i>gnashing teeth</i> attack first.</p><p><b>C: Flame breath +12 vs. PD (1d2 nearby enemies)</b> — 2d12 fire damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> Half damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>24</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>200</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Intellect Devourer

### Intellect Assassin

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>6<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Blocker</b></p><p><b>Aberration</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative +9</p><p><b>Formless fist +9 vs. PD (one enemy)</b> — 25 damage; OR if the target is fighting a <i>psychic duel</i> (see below), it can choose to take a –4 to penalty to its next check instead<br> <i>Quick use:</i> The assassin can take 15 damage to make this attack as a quick action (once per round).</p><p><b>C: Insidious domination +11 vs. MD (one enemy)</b> — 14 damage, and the opponent is locked in a <i>psychic duel</i> with the assassin (see below)</p><p><b>C: Mind thrust +10 vs. MD (one confused enemy)</b> — 35 damage (but only 50 damage on a crit)</p><p><i>Exploit trauma:</i> An intellect assassin’s crit range with attacks against MD expands by 2.</p><p><i>Lost opportunity:</i> This creature can’t make opportunity attacks.</p><p><i>Psychovore:</i> An intellect devourer remembers the current escalation die value the first time it becomes unhosted in a battle and gains a bonus equal to that value to all attacks and defenses until the end of the battle.</p><p><i>Psychic duel:</i> A psychic duel occurs when the intellect assassin hits with an <i>insidious domination</i> attack against a creature. At the start of the creature’s next turn, it must make an Intelligence skill check and can use a background that applies to psychic ability (if any). The result of this check determines that creature’s status until the start of its next turn. To maintain the psychic duel, the assassin must spend a move action each turn.</p><p><span>Psychic Duel Result: Status</span></p><p><b>15 or less:</b> The creature is confused until the end of its turn. It also can’t make opportunity attacks until the start of its next turn and takes a –2 penalty to its next <i>psychic duel</i> check.</p><p><b>16–22:</b> The creature is pressured—it takes a –2 penalty to attacks against any enemy except the assassin (dueling opponent).</p><p><b>23–27:</b> The creature steadies itself and can use a move action this turn to escape the <i>psychic duel</i>. If the creature chooses not to (or can’t) escape the duel, it gains a +2 bonus to its next <i>psychic duel</i> check.</p><p><b>28+:</b> As 23–27, but the creature takes advantage and gains a +4 bonus to its next <i>psychic duel</i> check instead of +2. In addition, the assassin takes a –2 penalty to attack rolls that target other creatures.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>90</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Intellect Devourer

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Aberration</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative +5</p><p><b>C: Recall trauma +8 vs. MD (one nearby enemy)</b> — 16 psychic damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target can’t add the escalation die to its attacks (save ends).</p><p><b>C: Ego scourge +8 vs. MD (one nearby or far away enemy)</b> — 10 psychic damage, and the target must choose one: take 10 extra damage; OR lose two points (cumulative) from its highest current background (min 0) until the next full heal-up</p><p><b>C: Mind wipe +10 vs. MD (one nearby enemy per point on esc. die)</b> — The target can neither detect the intellect devourer’s presence nor remember it was ever there to begin with. If no enemy in the battle remembers the devourer is there, remove it from play. Each nearby enemy immediately detects the devourer’s presence if it makes an attack or if it doesn’t leave the battle by the end of its next turn.<br> <i>Limited use:</i> 1/battle.</p><p><i>Exploit trauma:</i> The intellect devourer’s crit range with attacks against MD expands by 2.</p><p><i>Lost opportunity:</i> This creature can’t make opportunity attacks.</p><p><i>Psychovore:</i> An intellect devourer remembers the current escalation die value the first time its host body drops to 0 hit points in a battle and gains a bonus equal to that value to all attacks and defenses until the end of the battle.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Increased trauma:</i> Add the following extra effect trigger to the intellect devourer’s <i>recall trauma</i> attack.</p><p><i>Natural 5, 10, 15, 20:</i> The target can’t cast spells until the end of its next turn.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>56</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Jorogumo

### Binding Bride

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +8</p><p><b>Biting kiss +10 vs. AC</b> — 18 damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The target takes 10 ongoing poison damage.</p><p><b>Unwrapping my gift +10 vs. AC</b> — 18 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The binding bride can make a <i>biting kiss</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><b>R: A bouquet of webs +10 vs. PD (up to 2 enemies in a group)</b> — The target is hampered (save ends)</p><p><b>R: You ruined my special day +10 vs. MD</b> — The target takes 18 psychic damage each time it attacks the binding bride (save ends)<br> <i>Limited use:</i> 1/battle, as a quick action.</p><p><i>Give me your heart:</i> When the binding bride drops an enemy to 0 hit points or lower, she will move next to that creature as a free action and attempt to remove the target’s heart. The creature must begin making last gasp saves as she cuts its chest open. On the fourth failed save, the bride takes the heart and the target dies and becomes undead under her control. If the bride is stunned or moved away from the creature and can’t return to it on her turn, the creature doesn’t have to make a last gasp save that turn.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>72</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Lethal Lothario

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Leader</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +7</p><p><b>Brutal kiss +9 vs. AC</b> — 10 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> Any Woven engaged with the target can attack it as a free action.</p><p><b>C: Unhealthy attraction +9 vs. MD (nearby enemy with the fewest hit points)</b> — 10 psychic damage and the target is hampered until the end of the battle or until it takes one turn as if it were confused.<br> <i>Miss:</i> 5 ongoing psychic damage.</p><p><i>Give me your heart:</i> When the lothario drops an enemy to 0 hit points or lower, he will move next to that creature and attempt to remove the target’s heart. The creature must begin making last gasp saves as he cuts their chest open. On the fourth failure, the lothario takes the heart and the target dies and becomes undead under his control. If the lothario is stunned or moved away from the creature and can’t return to it on his turn, the creature doesn’t have to make a last gasp save that turn.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>50</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Spinneret Doxy

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +5</p><p><b>Bite of the love bug +8 vs. AC (or automatic critical hit vs. an <i>infatuated</i> enemy)</b> — 10 damage, and target is <i>infatuated</i> (save ends)<br> <i>Infatuated:</i> Infatuated enemies can’t attack the spinneret doxy or her Woven, but can convince themselves that other allies of the doxy don’t love her properly and should be slain. They also prattle on about how their friends shouldn’t attack her, but are too love-smitten to properly prevent it—they won’t attack their real allies.</p><p><b>R: Bring me flowers +8 vs. MD (one <i>infatuated</i> enemy)</b> — The target chooses one: it takes 6d6 psychic damage; OR as a free action, it moves next to the spinneret doxy (possibly provoking opportunity attacks), who engages it</p><p><b>C: Stop in the name of love +8 vs. MD (each nearby <i>infatuated</i> enemy)</b> — The target chooses one: it takes 6d6 psychic damage; OR it’s stuck (save ends)</p><p><i>Give me your heart:</i> When the doxy drops an enemy to 0 hit points or lower, she will move next to that creature and attempt to remove the target’s heart. ### The Woven

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +6</p><p><b>Clumsy strike +9 vs. AC</b> — 7 damage</p><p><b>R: Why aren’t you happy for ussss +8 vs. MD (1d3 nearby enemies)</b> — 5 psychic damage as the target’s mind reels against the horror of the truth</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>12</b></p><p><b>13</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Kobold

All kobolds have the _trapster_ ability. When a kobold makes a _trapster_ attack and rolls a natural attack roll that is higher than the target’s Wisdom, the creature has maneuvered the target into a trap with the attack. A creature can only be subjected to one trap per round.

When a kobold triggers its _trapster_ ability, determine the damage the trap deals by rolling a 1d4, then adding the escalation die. If there’s a dungeon-shaman in the battle, use a d8 instead of a d4.

Kobold traps can deal ongoing damage to the target instead of regular damage, if that makes sense for the trap. For ongoing damage, roll 1d4 (or 1d8) plus the escalation die, and then subtract one (minimum 1).

Kobold traps can impose conditions upon the target, if you choose. Roll normal trap damage, but the trap only deals half damage (minimum 1). Then roll a d4 for the condition the trap imposes upon the target until the end of its next turn.

1.  The target is stuck.
2.  The target is hampered.
3.  The target is dazed.
4.  The target is vulnerable.

Trap types vary according to the location/terrain and the whim of the GM.

### Kobold Archer

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>1<sup>st</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +4</p><p><b>Simple knife +6 vs. AC</b> — 3 damage</p><p><b>R: Tiny crossbow or javelin +7 vs. AC</b> — 3 damage</p><p><i>Evasive:</i> Kobolds take no damage from missed attacks.</p><p><i>Split off:</i> When one of the kobold’s allies engages a creature engaged with the kobold, the kobold can pop free as a free action.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>10</b></p><p><b>6</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Kobold Warrior

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>1<sup>st</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Troop</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +4</p><p><b>Spear +8 vs. AC</b> — 4 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The kobold warrior can pop free from the target.</p><p><i>Evasive:</i> Kobolds take no damage from missed attacks.</p><p><i>Not brave:</i> Kobold warriors with single digit hit points will run away the first chance they get.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>12</b></p><p><b>22</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Lammasu

_Flight:_ All lammasu fly. Warrior lammasu fly with upright dignity, sometimes a bit slower than is wise. Fallen lammasu fly well enough to keep up with all but the quickest demons. Lammasu wizards and priests fly more gracefully than the warriors, but only because they’re less eager to run into things.

_Minor servitors:_ When a lammasu isn’t in combat or resting in stone-form, it’s usually surrounded by a fawning retinue of spirit servants. The servants look like people from ages the world no longer remembers. They stick close to the lammasu, seldom or never speak, and in truth may be a projection of the lammasu’s spirit or will. The spirits are no use in combat, but they can manipulate small objects such as combs and scented perfumes to use upon the lammasu’s beard, hair, and jewelry.

_Stone rest:_ Outside the overworld, lammasu who wish to rest can transform themselves into solid stone. A lammasu can see and hear as if it were still made of flesh. It can change back to flesh as a free action, but must wait a day before returning to stone, which is no great delay for lammasu guardians whose positions extend for decades or centuries. Considering that many sculptors carve stone lammasu to place in front of or within important structures, it’s deliberately difficult for a thief or assassin to know whether he is facing a stone statue or a transformed beast.  
 Note that this form of solid stone is different from the living stone form sometimes adopted by the lammasu warrior, wizard, and priest during battle.

### Fallen Lammasu

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>7<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +11</p><p><b>Fiery hoof +12 vs. AC</b> — 30 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target takes 20 ongoing fire damage.<br> <i>Natural odd hit:</i> The fallen lammasu can make a second <i>fiery hoof</i> attack (but not a third) as a free action.</p><p><b>R: Rain of hellfire +11 vs. PD (1d4 random nearby creatures)</b> — 20 fire damage<br> <i>Natural even hit against an ally:</i> The target takes 10 ongoing fire damage instead of 20 fire damage, and until that ally saves against that damage, it adds the escalation die to its attacks.<br> <i>Natural even hit against an enemy:</i> The target also takes 15 ongoing fire damage.</p><p><i>Blessing of hellfire:</i> When the fallen lammasu fails a save against an effect created by an enemy, each enemy engaged with it takes 3d10 fire damage.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Curse of the fallen:</i> The lammasu gains an <i>Abyssal curse</i> attack.</p><p><b>C: Abyssal curse +12 vs. MD (one nearby enemy)</b> — The target takes 10 ongoing negative energy damage each time the fallen lammasu hits it with an attack (hard save ends, 16+)<br> <i>Limited use:</i> When the escalation die is odd, as a quick action (once per round).</p><p><i>The fire that burns:</i> When the fallen lammasu makes an attack that deals fire damage and the attack roll beats the target’s fire resistance, the target loses its fire resistance until the end of the battle.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>205</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

If it’s flying when it becomes living stone, its magic allows it to remain in the air if it wishes.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>On the crusade:</i> When an enemy misses the lammasu warrior with a melee attack, that enemy takes 2d10 damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>220</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Lammasu Wizard

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>2×</b></p><p><b>12<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +17</p><p><b>Draining bone rod +17 vs. AC</b> — 40 damage, 60 negative energy damage, and the target is dazed (hard save ends, 16+)<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target is weakened instead of dazed (hard save ends, 16+).<br> <i>Miss:</i> 40 damage.</p><p><b>R: Arcane blast +16 vs. PD (up to 3 nearby or far away enemies in a group)</b> — 50 force damage, and the target must roll a normal save; on a failure, it loses its next move action<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> Each enemy engaged with the lich prince pops free from it as a bubble of arcane energy pushes them away.</p><p><b>C: Soul rend +17 vs. PD (each nearby enemy)</b> — 30 negative energy damage, and ghostly hands reach up from the ground and grab the target (as they try to pull the target’s spirit out of its body)<br> <i>Ghostly grasping hands:</i> When a creature is being grabbed by the ghostly hands, it takes 30 negative energy damage at the start of its turn and must make a last gasp save. On the fourth failed last gasp save, the creature’s soul is torn from it and it dies. Unconscious creatures take a –4 penalty to their last gasp saves. It prefers to dig out a wide pit and lie in wait for prey. (See Burrowing.)</p><p><i>Can’t be blinded:</i> Between nictitating membranes that keep its eyes from being scratched out by the sand and its weird burrowing echolocation sense, the mantikumhar can’t be blinded.</p><p><i>Poison reservoirs:</i> Each time the mantikumhar uses its <i>serpent sting</i> attack, it takes 1d6 damage, or 2d6 damage if it’s staggered.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Hunker down:</i> A mantikumhar can burrow into the soil as a move action, concealing itself from attacks. ## Mummy

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>2×</b></p><p><b>8<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9<br>Vulnerability: fire</p><p><b>Unholy grasp +11 vs. PD</b> — 40 ongoing negative energy damage and the target is affected by <i>mummy rot</i> (save ends both)<br> <i>Each failed save (mummy rot):</i> The target’s flesh begins to rot and the ongoing damage increases by +40 (cumulative). Saves granted by special powers don’t increase this damage if they fail, only end of turn failures.<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The target also takes 20 damage.</p><p><b>C: Sepulchral glare +11 vs. MD (one nearby enemy)</b> — The target is hampered until the start of the mummy’s next turn<br> <i>Crit:</i> If the target is already affected by <i>mummy rot</i>, increase the ongoing negative energy damage by 40. If the target isn’t affected by <i>mummy rot</i> already, it takes 40 ongoing negative energy damage and is affected by <i>mummy rot</i> (save ends both)<br> <i>Limited use:</i> 1/round, as a quick action.</p><p><i>Mortal terror:</i> The presence of a mummy unnerves opponents, giving it an unusual <i>fear aura</i>. While engaged with this creature, enemies that have 200 hp or fewer are dazed (–4 attack) and do not add the escalation die to their attacks. Each time an enemy with 200 hp or fewer attacks the mummy, hit or miss, it must roll a save. On a success, it’s no longer affected by the <i>fear aura</i> effects of any mummy in the battle.</p><p><i>Spiritual grit:</i> When the mummy takes 20 damage or less from a non-fire attack, it takes no damage instead.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Blessing of preservation:</i> The mummy has a +4 bonus to all defenses until it takes damage.</p><p><i>Bone-chilling cry:</i> Once per battle as a quick action, the mummy can issue a bone-chilling cry that seems to echo from some unseen tomb or portal and it makes a <i>call of the sarcophagus</i> attack.</p><p><b>C: Call of the sarcophagus +11 vs. MD (each nearby enemy suffering <i>mummy rot</i>)</b> — The target is hampered until the end of its next turn</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>350</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Naga

Nastier Special for all naga

_Arcane balance:_ Whenever the naga rolls a natural 1–5 with an attack roll, it can cancel one magical effect created by a spell or magic item that is affecting the naga or a nearby creature (including beneficial effect on a PC). It can be an ongoing effect, an effect that only lasts a round, or even an effect that was supposed to last until the end of the battle. Use your sense of what is magical and what isn’t: a bard’s song is clearly magical, but a rogue’s Shadow Walk talent probably isn’t, despite the wizard’s arguments that it _should_ be.

### Elder Manafang Naga

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>10<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Leader</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +18</p><p><b>Bite +15 vs. AC</b> — 45 damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The naga gains <i>resist spell damage 16+</i> against the target’s spells until the end of the battle.<br> <i>Miss:</i> 25 damage.</p><p><b>R: Force missiles (1d4 nearby or far away enemies)</b> — 45 force damage<br> <i>Limited use:</i> 1/battle.</p><p><b>C: Ritual movements +15 vs. MD (one nearby enemy, or one nearby enemy per point of esc. die if <i>supreme mystic escalator</i> benefit is active)</b> — 45 psychic damage, and the target can’t cast spells or use the activated powers of true magic items (save ends)<br> <i>Miss:</i> 20 psychic damage.</p><p><i>Arcane mirror:</i> Whenever an enemy targets the elder manafang naga with a spell, the naga regains the use of <i>force missiles</i> if it’s expended. In addition, if that spell is a recharge spell, roll its recharge check immediately after the spell is cast. If the spell is a per-battle or daily spell, roll a hard save (16+) immediately after the spell is cast; on a success, the spellcaster doesn’t expend the spell.</p><p><i>Supreme mystic escalator:</i> The naga and each of its nearby allies can use the escalation die unless the naga has been hit by two enemy spells since its last turn.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>26</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>24</b></p><p><b>210</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Ogre

### Demonic Ogre

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup> level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Giant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +8</p><p><b>Demon-kissed blade +9 vs. AC</b> — 24 damage<br> <i>Natural 5, 10, 15, or 20:</i> The ogre gains a random <i>demonic advantage</i> (see below) until the end of the battle. All demonic advantages end if the ogre experiences a demonic eruption.<br> <i>Miss:</i> Half-damage.</p><p><b>R: Flaming spear +9 vs. AC</b> — 20 damage<br> <i>Natural 5, 10, 15, or 20:</i> The target takes 10 ongoing fire damage.</p><p><i>Demonic advantage:</i> Roll a d6 to determine which demonic ability the ogre gains.<br> 1: The ogre gains <i>resist energy 16+.</i><br> 2: Once per battle, the ogre can teleport anywhere it can see as a move action.<br> 3: The ogre’s attacks deal +1d8 damage, hit or miss.<br> 4: At the start of the ogre’s turn, each enemy engaged with it takes 2d6 negative energy damage.<br> 5: The ogre gains a +5 bonus to saves this battle.<br> 6: The ogre begins making <i>demonic eruption</i> rolls when the escalation die is 4+ instead of 6+.</p><p><i>Demonic eruption:</i> When the escalation die is 6+, the demonic ogre rolls a normal save at the start of each of its turns. On a success, roll a d6 and replace the demonic ogre with a new undamaged demon. 1–2: Imp; 3–4: Despoiler; 5: Frenzy demon; 6: Cambion sickle.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Early eruption:</i> Begin making <i>demonic eruption </i>rolls when the escalation die is 5+ instead of 6+. Also use stronger demons for the options that the ogre could turn into.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>100</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Ogre

### Ogre Berserker

### Ogre Champion

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Giant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +10</p><p><b>Champion’s battle-axe +10 vs. AC</b> — 30 damage<br> <i>Natural 5, 10, 15, or 20:</i> The ogre champion gains a second standard action this turn, but not a third.<br> <i>Miss:</i> Half damage.</p><p><b>R: Heavy javelin +10 vs. AC (one nearby or far away enemy)</b> — 26 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 10 damage.</p><p><i>Racial enemies:</i> Whenever a nearby dwarf or elf enemy attempts to use their racial power, they must roll a hard save (16+). On a failure, the power fails and has no effect that turn (but they can try again next turn).</p><p><i>Slayer of wizards:</i> Creatures engaged with the ogre champion take opportunity attacks from it when casting close spells as if they were casting ranged spells.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Escalating danger:</i> The ogre champion adds the escalation die to the damage it deals with its attacks, hit or miss.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>140</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Ogre Mage

### Ogre Lightning Mage

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>8<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Caster</b></p><p><b>Giant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +15</p><p><b>Naginata +14 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 40 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 15 damage.</p><p><b>R: Lightning from torn sky +14 vs. PD (up to 2 nearby enemies, plus one far away enemy, if any)</b> — 52 lightning damage<br> <i>Limited use:</i> 1/battle, but the ogre lightning mage regains the use of this attack if it’s expended each time it uses its <i>naginata</i> attack.</p><p><b>R: Past master’s judgment +14 vs. MD (1d3 nearby enemies)</b> — 25 psychic damage<br> <i>First natural even hit each attack:</i> The ogre lightning mage can cancel one spell or magical effect created by the target.</p><p><i>Flight:</i> The ogre lightning mage flies well using the sheer power of its superior mind.</p><p><i>Invisibility:</i> While not engaged, the ogre lightning mage can turn invisible as an at-will standard action. It becomes visible when it attacks. The ogre mage takes 1d10 damage each time it uses <i>invisibility</i> while it’s staggered.</p><p><i>Resist exceptional attacks 16+:</i> When a limited attack (not an at-will attack) targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 16+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><i>Trollish regeneration 20:</i> While an ogre mage is damaged, its uncanny flesh heals 20 hit points at the start of the ogre mage’s turn. It can regenerate five times per battle. If it heals to its maximum hit points, then that use of <i>regeneration</i> doesn’t count against the five-use limit.<br> When the ogre mage is hit by an attack that deals fire or acid damage, it loses one use of its <i>regeneration</i>, and it can’t regenerate during its next turn.<br> Dropping an ogre mage to 0 hp doesn’t kill it if it has any uses of <i>regeneration</i> left.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>24</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>230</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Ogre Mage

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>7<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Caster</b></p><p><b>Giant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +14</p><p><b>Naginata +13 vs. AC</b> — 35 damage<br> <i>Natural 18+:</i> Make a second <i>naginata</i> attack against a nearby enemy as a free action (engaging it is not required)</p><p><b>C: Cone of cold +13 vs. PD (up to 3 nearby enemies in a group)</b> — 50 cold damage<br> <i>Limited use:</i> 1/day, and the attack affects the ogre’s allies engaged with or between enemy targets.</p><p><i>Aura of treachery:</i> Once per round when a nearby enemy misses the ogre mage with an attack, the ogre mage can make an <i>aura of treachery</i> attack against it as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: Aura of treachery +13 vs. MD</b> — The target is confused until the end of the ogre mage’s next turn</p><p><i>Flight:</i> The ogre mage flies using the sheer power of its superior mind.</p><p><i>Invisibility:</i> If the ogre mage is not engaged, it can turn invisible as an at-will standard action. It becomes visible when it attacks. The ogre mage takes 1d10 damage each time it uses <i>invisibility</i> while it’s staggered.</p><p><i>Resist exceptional attacks 16+:</i> When a limited attack (not an at-will attack) targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 16+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><i>Trollish regeneration 20:</i> While an ogre mage is damaged, its uncanny flesh heals 20 hit points at the start of the ogre mage’s turn. It can regenerate five times per battle. If it heals to its maximum hit points, then that use of <i>regeneration</i> doesn’t count against the five-use limit.<br> When the ogre mage is hit by an attack that deals fire or acid damage, it loses one use of its <i>regeneration</i>, and it can’t regenerate during its next turn.<br> Dropping an ogre mage to 0 hp doesn’t kill it if it has any uses of <i>regeneration</i> left.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>170</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Ogre Mage Knight

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>6<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Giant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +13</p><p><b>Naginata +11 vs. AC</b> — The effect depends on the roll.<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> 25 damage, and the ogre mage knight can use <i>lightning pulse</i> as a free action.<br> <i>Natural odd hit:</i> 20 damage, and the ogre mage knight can use <i>voice of thunder</i> as a free action.<br> <i>Natural even miss:</i> 10 damage, and the ogre mage knight can teleport to any nearby location it can see before using <i>magi’s lightning chain</i> as a free action.<br> <i>Natural odd miss:</i> The ogre mage knight can use <i>cone of cold</i> as a free action.</p><p><b>R: Magi’s lightning chain +11 vs. PD</b> — 15 lightning damage, and each time this attack has a natural even attack roll, the ogre mage knight can target a different creature with the ability</p><p><b>C: Cone of cold +11 vs. PD (up to 3 nearby enemies in a group, also targets the ogre’s allies engaged with the targets)</b> — 20 cold damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 10 cold damage.</p><p><b>C: Lightning pulse +11 vs. PD (one random nearby or far away enemy)</b> — 20 lightning damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target is weakened (save ends).</p><p><b>C: Voice of thunder +11 vs. PD (1d3 nearby enemies)</b> — 15 thunder damage</p><p><i>Resist exceptional attacks 16+:</i> When a limited attack (not an at-will attack) targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 16+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><i>Trollish regeneration 15:</i> While an ogre mage is damaged, its uncanny flesh heals 15 hit points at the start of the ogre mage’s turn. It can regenerate five times per battle. If it heals to its maximum hit points, then that use of <i>regeneration</i> doesn’t count against the five-use limit.<br> When the ogre mage is hit by an attack that deals fire or acid damage, it loses one use of its <i>regeneration</i>, and it can’t regenerate during its next turn.<br> Dropping an ogre mage to 0 hp doesn’t kill it if it has any uses of <i>regeneration</i> left.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Ki:</i> Gain 1d4 ki at the start of each battle. Spend a point of ki as a free action, once per round, to change the ogre mage knight’s natural attack result by one; a natural 1 could become a 2, a natural 19 could become a natural 20, and so on.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>160</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Prismatic Ogre Mage

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>9<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Caster</b></p><p><b>Giant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +16</p><p><b>Horns and claws +15 vs. AC</b> — 75 damage<br> <i>Natural 2–5:</i> The prismatic ogre mage can use <i>prismatic blast</i> as a free action without provoking an opportunity attack.</p><p><b>Force shove +15 vs. PD (each enemy engaged with ogre)</b> — 10 force damage, and the target pops free from the ogre mage<br> <i>Quick use:</i> This power only requires a quick action (once per round) instead of a standard action when the escalation die is odd.</p><p><b>R: Prismatic blast +15 vs. PD (1d3 nearby or far away enemies in a group)</b> — Roll a d8 against each hit target to determine the type of ray and effect<br> <i>1. Red:</i> 75 fire damage; <i>Miss:</i> 40 fire damage.<br> <i>2. Orange:</i> 50 damage, and the target is confused (save ends).<br> <i>3. Yellow:</i> 40 ongoing poison damage.<br> <i>4. Green:</i> The target loses a recovery, and the prismatic ogre mage heals 70 hp.<br> <i>5. Blue:</i> 60 lightning damage, and make a secondary attack:<br>  <b>+15 vs. PD (one enemy near the target)</b> — 20 lightning damage.<br> <i>6. Cyan:</i> The target is stunned (save ends).<br> <i>7. Purple:</i> The target is dazed and confused (save ends both). When the target saves, it takes 40 psychic damage.<br>&nbsp;<i>8. Magenta:</i> The target is transported into the future. Remove that creature from play, returning it to the battle in (or near) its previous location at the end of its next turn. No time seems to pass for the target while it’s gone.</p><p><i>Resist exceptional attacks 16+:</i> When a limited attack (not an at-will attack) targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 16+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.</p><p><i>Warp:</i> The prismatic ogre mage warps reality with its presence. Each character hit by the <i>prismatic blast</i> attack during battle must write down one true personal trait or preference about their character such as: “Yellow hair”, “Afraid of spiders”, “Prefers white wine to red”, or “Tattoo of a halfling on left bicep”. These personal traits are shuffled and randomly distributed equally by the GM after the battle is over. Whichever trait each player receives is now true for their character as well as for the character of the player who wrote it down (unless there has somehow turned out to be a swap…). These traits don’t alter game mechanics (feats, powers, backgrounds, icon relationships, attributes, bonuses, etc.). They are personal details that have been warped and scrambled by the prismatic ogre mage’s magic.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>25</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>360</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Ooze

All oozes have the following two abilities:

_Flows where it likes:_ The ooze is immune to opportunity attacks.

_Ooze:_ The ooze is immune to effects. When an attack applies a condition to an ooze (dazed, hampered, weakened, ongoing damage, etc.), that condition doesn’t affect it.

### Black Pudding

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Huge</b></p><p><b>9<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Ooze</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +8</p><p><b>C: Acid-drenched pseudopod +14 vs. PD (up to 4 attacks, each against a different nearby enemy)</b> — 30 acid damage, and 10 ongoing acid damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 10 acid damage.</p><p><i>Climber:</i> A black pudding sticks to ceilings and walls when it wishes, sliding along as easily as on the floor.</p><p><i>Slippery:</i> The pudding has <i>resist weapons 12+</i>.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>470</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>
