### Death-Plague Orc

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +2</p><p><b>Huge spiked flail +8 vs. AC</b> — 21 damage<br> <i>Natural roll is above target’s Constitution:</i> The target catches a disease (see below).</p><p>When a creature contracts a death-plague orc disease, roll a d4 for the disease type and a d6 for that disease’s symptoms <i>after the battle</i>. Until cured, at the start of each day (after each full heal-up) the PC makes a Constitution check (including any appropriate background) to determine the severity of the disease for that day, or if the PC is cured.<br> Full bed rest under the care of a healer reduces severity roll from a d6 to a d4 (so a severity check result of 18 would be 1d4 + 2 not 1d6 + 2). A PC under the care of and experience healer or someone who knows healing magic gains a +10 bonus to the Constitution check. At the GM’s option, special ingredients or healing items, found via quest, can give additional bonuses to the check.</p><p>Disease Type (d4)<br> 1: Filthy Fever<br> 2: Chatter Pox<br> 3: Slug Scourge<br> 4: Red Fever</p><p>Disease Severity (Con check each day; result affects d6 symptoms roll)<br> 1–14: d6 + 3<br> 15–19: d6 + 2<br> 20–24: d6 + 1<br> 25–29: d6 + 0<br> 30+: Cured</p><p>Filthy Fever Symptoms (d6 roll for symptoms that day)<br> 1: Slight temperature.<br> 2–3: The runs. You gain 1 less recovery than normal after a full heal-up due to fluid loss.<br> 4+: You have a hacking cough that sounds like insane laughter and are losing fluids. You gain 2 fewer recoveries than normal after a full heal-up and can’t remain silent.</p><p>Chatter Pox Symptoms (d6 roll for symptoms that day)<br> 1: Unsightly and painful sores, occasional shivers.<br> 2–3: Running sores, shivering and chattering teeth. You take a –3 penalty to social skill checks and to attack rolls with spells.<br> 4+: Infected sores, fever dreams. Your constitution is weakened. After each full heal-up, roll 1d4 + 3 to determine your starting maximum recoveries for that day. Each time you cast a spell that isn’t at-will, there’s a 25% chance it fails (but you don’t expend the spell).</p><p>Slug Scourge Symptoms (d6 roll for symptoms that day)<br> 1: Extreme appetite, nausea.<br> 2–3: Vomiting up slugs. Whenever you make a non-combat Charisma check, roll 2d20 and take the lower result.<br> 4+: The slugs are inside your lungs! After each quick rest, you lose 25% of your maximum hit points. If you drop to 0 hp this way, you enter into a coma until the next day.</p><p>Red Fever Symptoms (d6 roll for symptoms that day)<br> 1: Scarlet stripes on the eyeballs, itching, buzzing in ears.<br> 2–3: Blurred vision. You take a –3 penalty to ranged attacks.<br> 4+: Fever, rage, and confusion. Whenever you roll a natural odd attack roll, you are confused until the end of your next turn. Ranged attacks have a 25% chance of accidentally targeting an ally (check before making the attack roll).</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>12</b></p><p><b>90</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Otyugh

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Blocker</b></p><p><b>Aberration</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +5</p><p><b>Grasping tentacles +8 vs. PD (2 attacks)</b> — 5 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The otyugh can grab the target.<br> <i>Natural 18 or 20:</i> The otyugh can grab the target and make a <i>big toothy maw</i> attack against it as a free action.</p><p><b>Big toothy maw +12 vs. AC (one enemy it’s grabbing; includes +4 grab bonus)</b> — 16 damage</p><p><i>Trash nest defense:</i> The otyugh gains a +2 bonus to all defenses while fighting in its nest or in similar piles of excrement and trash.</p><p><i>Tentacle flail:</i> Once per round, an otyugh can make a <i>grasping tentacles</i> attack as a free action against a moving nearby creature it is not engaged with; on a natural even hit, the target is grabbed and its movement stops.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>84</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Owlbear

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th<sup>&nbsp;level</sup></sup></b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +8</p><p><b>Rip and peck +9 vs. AC</b> — 15 damage, and until the end of the owlbear’s next turn, the target is hampered (<i>makes only basic attacks</i>) while engaged with the owlbear<br> <i>Vicious hybrid:</i> If the escalation die is even, make another <i>rip and peck</i> attack.</p><p><i>Feed the cubs:</i> An owlbear that scores a critical hit against a hampered enemy tears a piece of the creature off (GM chooses a limb) and will subsequently attempt to retreat with the prize to feed its cubs. The torn-up enemy is stunned until the end of its next turn.</p><p><i>Silent hunter:</i> Owlbears are nearly silent until they strike. Checks to hear them approaching take a –5 penalty.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>101</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Phase Spider

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>7<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +16</p><p><b>Phasing fangs +11 vs. PD (2 attacks)</b> — 25 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The spider can make a <i>rummage and filch</i> attack against the target as a free action, even if the target isn’t staggered.</p><p><b>Rummage and filch +11 vs. MD (one staggered creature)</b> — The phase spider steals a random true magic item from the target (see below).</p><p><i>Phasing abilities:</i> As long as it didn’t just return from being out of phase, at the start of the phase spider’s turn, roll a d6 to see which of its phase and teleport abilities it can access that turn. The spider doesn’t have to use the available ability and can attack normally, if it wishes.</p><p><b>1–2:</b> <i>Short teleport</i> — As a move action, the spider can teleport anywhere it can see nearby.</p><p><b>3:</b> <i>Long teleport</i> — As a move action, the spider can teleport anywhere it can see nearby or far away.</p><p><b>4–5:</b> <i>Phase out</i> — As a move action, the spider can remove itself from the battlefield, returning on its next initiative turn anywhere it chooses nearby. It doesn’t get to make a phase roll at the start of its next turn though.</p><p><b>6:</b> <i>Teleport away</i> — If the spider has stolen at least one magic item, as a move action it can teleport back to its lair, or to its master if it has one. It leaves the battle. If it hasn’t stolen an item yet, it won’t leave and can use its choice of the other abilities this turn.</p><p><i>Stolen items:</i> If the spider is slain before it leaves battle, all items stolen from the party are recovered. If a d20 roll results in a 20, other magic items are found.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>200</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Pixie

All pixies have the _glamour_ ability.

_Glamour:_ Outside of combat, pixies can create complex illusions at will. For the PC, it’s usually a normal or hard skill check to sort out what’s real.

### Pixie Warrior

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +12</p><p><b>Diminutive sparkly sword +8 vs. PD</b> — 5 psychic damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The pixie warrior can make a <i>madness</i> attack against the target as a free action.</p><p><b>R: Enchanted bowshot +8 vs. PD</b> — 4 psychic damage, and the pixie warrior can make a <i>madness</i> attack against the target as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>Madness +8 vs. MD</b> — The target is maddened until the end of the pixie’s next turn. The first thing the creature does on its turn is use a standard action to make a display of power that has no practical benefit. The GM chooses the attack, spell, or other power, which should be the most powerful one the character has, preferably a daily. The target expends the power in a great show of prowess, aimed for display rather than effect. Wizards cast their fireballs into the sky, monks demonstrate flawless form while shadow-boxing, and clerics bless the very stones underfoot instead of allies.<br> When the madness effect gets old, substitute any of the following effects, by choice or at random:</p><p><i>1:</i> You love pixies and hate those who threaten them. The target is confused until the end of the pixie’s next turn.</p><p><i>2:</i> Brains knocked loose. The target takes 4 psychic damage each time it takes an action (save ends; yes that could be 3 times per round or more).</p><p><i>3:</i> Reality bender. The target takes 5 ongoing psychic damage. Each time the target fails the save, the ongoing damage increases by 5, cumulative.</p><p><i>4:</i> Massive attack on the unconscious mind. The target chooses one: either let the onslaught slam its mind (take 15 psychic damage), or steel its mind against the onslaught (stunned until the end of the pixie’s next turn).</p><p><i>5:</i> Compulsion to dance. The target takes 5 ongoing psychic damage (no save) until it spends a standard action to dance maniacally. Dancing ends all such ongoing damage, even if the target has been hit multiple times with this effect.</p><p><i>6:</i> Pacifism. The target can’t attack until the end of the pixie’s next turn.</p><p><i>Dazzling lights:</i> During battle, pixies fill the air with the light and sound of countless flashy illusions. The effects are disorienting enough that the PCs don’t get to add the escalation die to their attacks.</p><p><i>Flight:</i> Pixies make flying look like a lot of fun.</p><p><i>Invisibility:</i> When an enemy attacks a pixie and misses, the pixie turns invisible until the start of its next turn (even if it makes opportunity attacks). A pixie can also turn invisible as a standard action, in which case the invisibility still lasts until the start of its next turn.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>24</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Predatory Plant

### Claw Flower

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>2<sup>nd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Plant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +6</p><p><b>Serrated claw +7 vs. AC</b> — 8 damage<br> <i>Natural 1–5:</i> The claw flower takes 1d4 damage from burst roots.</p><p><b>C: Bumble spores +4 vs. MD (1d2 nearby random non-plant creatures)</b> — The effect depends on the roll<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> 4 psychic damage, and the target is confused until end of its next turn.<br> <i>Natural odd hit:</i> 3 psychic damage, and the target is stuck until end of its next turn.<br> <i>Miss:</i> 2 psychic damage.</p><p><i>Immobile until pressed:</i> The claw flower has roots and normally can’t move, but when it takes 10 or more damage from a single attack it can move normally during its next turn.</p><p><i>Spore escalator:</i> The claw flower adds the escalation die to its <i>bumble spores</i> attack rolls.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Gentle roar:</i> Once per battle, the claw flower can make a <i>bumble spores</i> attack as a quick action.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>12</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>40</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Pixie Pod

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>2×</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Leader</b></p><p><b>Plant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +7</p><p><b>C: Peripheral summoning +8 vs. MD (one random nearby enemy)</b> — 8 psychic damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> Add a new podling into the battle in a random location.</p><p><i>Release the pods:</i> Once per battle when the pixie pod rolls a natural even hit with peripheral summoning, it adds a number of podlings into the battle equal to the escalation die instead of only one.</p><p><i>Immobile:</i> Although its podlings occasionally pick up and move it around out of combat, in battle the pixie pod can’t move and is stuck except for its teleport ability.</p><p><i>Lost opportunity:</i> This creature can’t make opportunity attacks.</p><p><i>Lurching teleport:</i> Once per battle as a move action, the pixie-pod can teleport to a nearby location. But its control sucks. The teleport goes in a random direction. Roll it using a d8 for direction.</p><p><i>Magical concealment:</i> As long as one or more of its podlings are nearby, the pixie pod is invisible and extremely difficult to even detect. A PC who wants to locate the pixie-pod must spend a standard action searching and succeed at a DC 25 skill check using Wisdom. Backgrounds connected to plants and the wilderness help normally, and general searching skills and magic talents might help a bit but not at full strength. Once located, the plant can be attacked like a normal invisible creature. When it teleports, however, it must be located all over again.</p><p><i>Start with mooks:</i> The pixie pod is normally accompanied by five active podlings that don’t count toward the total when building a battle with the pod. Additional podlings do count, however.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>40</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Podling

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Plant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9</p><p><b>Needle sword +8 vs. AC</b> — 6 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target can’t choose to search for the pixie-pod plant until all podlings in the battle are slain.</p><p><b>R: Tiny green bow +8 vs. AC</b> — 5 damage</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Flight:</i> The podling that can fly, hovering out of reach and firing arrows, can be a real pain in the pate.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>10</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Purple Worm

### Ancient Purple Worm

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Huge</b></p><p><b>12<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +17</p><p><b>Devouring maw +18 vs. PD</b> — 100 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target is swallowed whole if it’s smaller than the worm (see below).<br> <i>Miss:</i> Half damage.</p><p><b>Tail sting +18 vs. AC (up to 2 random nearby enemies)</b> — 40 damage, and 40 ongoing poison damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 20 damage.</p><p><b>Prodigious thrash +18 vs. AC (1d4 random nearby enemies)</b> — 50 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> Half damage.<br> <i>Natural 1–2:</i> The worm and any creatures it has swallowed take 8d6 damage (but it still deals miss damage on a 2).<br> <i>Limited use:</i> The worm can make this attack as a free action if it has one enemy swallowed or less after using its standard action during its turn.</p><p><i>Swallow whole:</i> While a creature is swallowed whole, it takes 10d12 acid damage at the start of its turn and is stuck, hampered, and unable to attack or affect anything outside the worm’s stomach (and vice-versa). Most teleport abilities don’t work because you’re hampered <i>and</i> you can’t see the location out of the worm you want to teleport to. There are two ways out.<br> <b>Cut your way out:</b> Deal 80 damage to the worm with a single attack and you can cut your way out. All edged or bladed weapons are reduced to d6 damage dice (at most) inside the worm’s gullet, so good luck. At least you’ll be damaging the worm attacking it from within.<br> <b>Get upchucked:</b> While the worm is staggered, you can use a standard action to try and crawl out of its mouth. Roll a hard save (16+); on a success, the worm vomits you out and spits you somewhere nearby. The worm also vomits out all creatures it has swallowed when it drops to 0 hp.</p><p><i>Burrow:</i> As the standard monster ability, but with a +5 bonus to the check.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Resist most energy damage 16+:</i> Purple worms generate weird energy resistances thanks to underworld radiation and their odd diets. Roll a d8 twice, in secret, to determine what energy types the worm is not resistant to. The PCs probably have to find out what energy works best against the worm the hard way, though you might have mercy and allow a DC 35 Wisdom skill check to figure out what energy types work against the worm.<br> <b>1:</b> acid; <b>2:</b> cold; <b>3:</b> fire; <b>4:</b> lightning; <b>5:</b> thunder; <b>6:</b> holy; <b>7:</b> negative energy; <b>8:</b> poison.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>27</b></p><p><b>25</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>1200</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Parasitic Lightning Beetle

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>8<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +14</p><p><b>Mouthparts +12 vs. AC</b> — 10 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The target also takes 5 lightning damage.</p><p><b>R: Lightning zap +12 vs. PD (one nearby enemy not engaged with a purple worm, purple larvae, or parasitic beetle)</b> — 20 lightning damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The target takes 5 extra lightning damage.</p><p><i>Flight:</i> The beetles fly badly, usually just enough to get back to the worm when they’ve been shaken off from their hiding spots in its segments.</p><p><i>Scaredy bugs:</i> Whenever one or more parasitic lightning beetles drop to 0 hp, roll a d6. If you roll less than or equal to the number of beetles that were destroyed by that attack, all beetles in the battle stop fighting, using all their actions during their next turn to disengage and fly away.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>27</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>36</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Purple Larva

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>8<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9</p><p><b>Bitey maw +13 vs. AC</b> — 20 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The larvae can make a <i>tail sting</i> attack against a random enemy engaged with it as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>Tail sting +13 vs. AC</b> — 5 damage, and 10 ongoing poison damage</p><p><i>Merge with worm:</i> Purple larvae can dig quickly in and out of the skin of the purple worm as if they were burrowing but without needing die rolls to succeed.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>44</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Purple Worm

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Huge</b></p><p><b>8<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +11</p><p><b>Devouring maw +13 vs. PD</b> — 50 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target is swallowed whole if it’s smaller than the worm (see below).<br> <i>Miss:</i> Half damage.</p><p><b>Tail sting +13 vs. AC (one random nearby enemy)</b> — 20 damage, and 20 ongoing poison damage</p><p><b>C: Mighty thrash +13 vs. AC (1d3 random nearby enemies)</b> — 30 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> Half damage.<br> <i>Natural 1–5:</i> The worm takes 10 damage (but it still deals miss damage on a 2–5).<br> <i>Limited use:</i> The worm can make this attack as a free action if it has no enemies swallowed after using its standard action during its turn.</p><p><i>Swallow whole:</i> While a creature is swallowed whole, it takes 7d10 acid damage at the start of its turn and is stuck, hampered, and unable to attack or affect anything outside the worm’s stomach (and vice-versa). Most teleport abilities don’t work because you’re hampered <i>and</i> you can’t see the location out of the worm you want to teleport to. There are two ways out.<br> <b>Cut your way out:</b> Deal 40 damage to the worm with a single attack and you can cut your way out. All edged or bladed weapons are reduced to d6 damage dice (at most) inside the worm’s gullet, so good luck. At least you’ll be damaging the worm attacking it from within.<br> <b>Get upchucked:</b> While the worm is staggered, you can use a standard action to try and crawl out of its mouth. Roll a hard save (16+); on a success, the worm vomits you out and spits you somewhere nearby. The worm also vomits out all creatures it has swallowed when it drops to 0 hp.</p><p><i>Burrow:</i> As the standard monster ability.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Larval feeding:</i> The worm’s stomach also includes a mob of larval mooks (purple larvae or parasitic lightning beetles). Feel free to add this nastier special if a PC acts dismissive about the possibility of being swallowed by the worm.</p><p><i>Resist most energy damage 16+:</i> Purple worms generate weird energy resistances thanks to underworld radiation and their odd diets. Roll a d8 twice, in secret, to determine what energy types the worm is not resistant to. The PCs probably have to find out what energy works best against the worm the hard way, though you might have mercy and allow a DC 35 Wisdom skill check to figure out what energy types work against the worm.<br> <b>1:</b> acid; <b>2:</b> cold; <b>3:</b> fire; <b>4:</b> lightning; <b>5:</b> thunder; <b>6:</b> holy; <b>7:</b> negative energy; <b>8:</b> poison.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>440</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Rakshasa

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>2×</b></p><p><b>8<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Caster</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +16</p><p><b>Claws and bite +11 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 25 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The rakshasa can make a <i>rend mind</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><b>R: Striped lightning bolts +13 vs. PD (1d3 nearby enemies)</b> — 25 lightning damage, or 50 lightning damage against a staggered target<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The rakshasa can make a <i>rend mind</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><b>C: Rend mind +13 vs. MD (one nearby enemy)</b> — 15 psychic damage, and the target is confused (<i>make a basic or at-will attack vs. ally</i>) until the end of the rakshasa’s next turn</p><p><i>Shapechange:</i> As a standard action, the rakshasa can change its form to that of any humanoid, or back to its own shape. Seeing through the shapechange requires a DC 25 skill check.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Master of chaos:</i> The rakshasa gains a bonus to all defenses equal to the current number of confused enemies in the battle.</p><p><i>Reversal of fate:</i> Once per day as a quick action, the rakshasa steals the escalation die; until the end of the battle, the rakshasa gains an attack bonus equal to the die’s value when it was stolen. Reset the escalation die to 0 for the players and increase it normally with each new round.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>280</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Redcap

All redcaps have special abilities based on _The Bad Word_. Before every battle against redcaps, the GM should determine the _bad word_ for that battle. Whenever a PC or a player at the table says the word, every redcap in the battle can use their associated ability as a free action that interrupts whatever action is currently happening.

### Crimsoncap

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>6<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +11</p><p><b>Huge bloody cleavers +11 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 13 damage, and the crimsoncap can pop free from the target</p><p><b>Horrible stompy boots +11 vs. PD (one staggered or unconscious enemy)</b> — 20 damage, and the target is hampered (save ends)<br> <i>Miss:</i> 5 damage.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: Pop-out and slash ‘em +11 vs. AC (1d4 nearby enemies)</b> — 15 damage, and 5 ongoing damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 10 damage.</p><p><i>Impossible teleport:</i> When the crimsoncap scores a critical hit OR when a PC or a player at the table says the <i>bad word</i>, the crimsoncap can teleport to a nearby hidden location it can see or can’t see (like inside a closet) as a free action.</p><p><i>Pop-out surprise:</i> When the crimsoncap starts its turn and no enemy can see it, it can make a <i>pop-out and slash ’em</i> attack that turn as a standard action</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>F*** T***:</i> The crimsoncap has two <i>bad words</i> instead of one. And the PCs find that out the hard way. Write the words down ahead of time to prove you’re not <i>just</i> being a mean GM.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>84</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Crustycap

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>7<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +14</p><p><b>Big bloody axe +12 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 10 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The crustycap can make a single <i>big bloody axe</i> attack against a different nearby enemy as a free action.<br> <i>Miss:</i> 5 ongoing damage.</p><p><b>Devastating stompy boots +12 vs. PD (one staggered or unconscious enemy)</b> — 40 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 10 damage.</p><p><i>Oh no oh no:</i> When a PC or a player at the table says the <i>bad word</i>, the crustycap can take an extra standard action during its next turn. Feel free to let the extra actions stack a few times if someone gets cocky.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Just plain mean:</i> When the crustycap scores a critical hit OR when a PC or a player at the table says the <i>bad word</i>, the crustycap can teleport away as a free action. Far away, even to a location it can’t see, and out of the battle. Then at the start of the PCs’ next battle, it teleports back and attacks the PCs, no matter what enemies they are fighting. It will continue to use this power if it can until the PCs take a full heal-up, at which point, if it’s still alive, it loses interest.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>100</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Redcap

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9</p><p><b>Twin skinning knives +8 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 6 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> Damage equal to the escalation die.</p><p><b>Stompy iron boots +8 vs. PD (one staggered or unconscious enemy)</b> — 12 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 5 damage.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: Pop-out and ride ‘em +10 vs. AC (one nearby enemy)</b> — 10 damage, and 5 ongoing damage<br> <i>Ridey-horsey:</i> While the target is taking ongoing damage from this attack, the redcap is riding the target’s shoulders with its knives in the target’s ears, and once during its turn the redcap can use a move action to make the target move anywhere nearby that won’t directly cause it harm (but opportunity attacks are fair game).<br> <i>Miss:</i> 5 damage.</p><p><i>Impossible teleport:</i> When the redcap scores a critical hit OR when a PC or a player at the table says the <i>bad word</i>, the redcap can teleport to a nearby hidden location it can see as a free action.</p><p><i>Pop-out surprise:</i> When the redcap starts its turn and no enemy can see it, it can make a <i>pop-out and ride ‘em</i> attack that turn as a standard action</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>42</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Splotchcap

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>2<sup>nd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Archer</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +8</p><p><b>Stabby knife +5 vs. AC</b> — 6 damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The target also takes 2 ongoing damage.</p><p><b>R: Smashy slingstone +7 vs. AC</b> — 7 damage<br> <i>Natural 18+:</i> The target can’t cast a spell until the end of its next turn or until the splotchcap drops to 0 hp, whichever comes first.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: Pop-out and stab ‘em +7 vs. AC (one nearby enemy)</b> — 8 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> Damage equal to the escalation die.</p><p><i>Impossible teleport:</i> When the splotchcap scores a critical hit OR when a PC or a player at the table says the <i>bad word</i>, the splotchcap can teleport to a nearby hidden location it can see as a free action.</p><p><i>Pop-out surprise:</i> When the splotchcap starts its turn and no enemy can see it, it can make a <i>pop-out and stab ‘em</i> attack that turn as a standard action.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>32</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Remorhaz

### Adult Remorhaz

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>8<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +11</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: Death from below! +14 vs. AC (each nearby creature)</b> — 45 damage; OR 22 damage, and the target is stunned (save ends)<br> <i>Miss:</i> 15 damage.<br> <i>Limited use:</i> 1/battle, during the remorhaz’s first turn or if appearing on the surface after burrowing.</p><p><b>Savage bite +16 vs. AC</b> — 50 damage, 20 fire damage, and the remorhaz grabs the target if it’s not already grabbing a creature<br> <i>Miss:</i> 15 fire damage.</p><p><i>Burrow:</i> As the standard monster ability, except the remorhaz only needs to roll 6+ in snow and ice.</p><p><i>Furnace aura:</i> When a creature is engaged with the remorhaz (or grabbed by it) at the start of its turn, it takes fire damage equal to 6 × the escalation die.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Bejeweled remorhaz:</i> The remorhaz has glowing “jewels” on its armored plates. When a nearby or far away enemy misses with an attack against the remorhaz, that enemy chooses one: It takes 10 fire damage; OR one piece of its non-magical equipment (something useful, but player’s choice) melts or burns up. Adjust skill checks or stats accordingly.</p><p><i>Remorhaz steamer:</i> The remorhaz is melting the ice/snow all the time and obscuring steam rises into the air. Ranged attacks against the remorhaz take a –2 penalty, or a –4 penalty if the attacker is far away.</p><p><i>Spiney remorhaz:</i> The remorhaz is covered in red-hot spines. When a nearby enemy rolls a natural 1–5 with an attack roll, it takes 20 fire damage unless it has somehow protected itself from the heat.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>24</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>280</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Barbellite

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Troop</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +7</p><p><b>Arctic bite +11 vs. AC</b> — 7 cold damage</p><p><i>Heat absorption:</i> When a creature is engaged with the remorhaz at the start of its turn, it takes cold damage equal to the escalation die.</p><p><i>Shatterer:</i> Death can cause fluid-filled sacks inside the barbellite to explode. When the attack roll that kills the barbellite is a natural even roll, each nearby creature takes 10 cold damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>12</b></p><p><b>36</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Frost-Würm

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>6<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Troop</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9</p><p><b>Würm glaciation +11 vs. AC</b> — 18 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target and one other nearby enemy takes 18 cold damage as the area freezes over.<br> <i>Miss:</i> The target and one other nearby enemy takes 6 cold damage.</p><p><b>Trilling vibrations +9 vs. MD (1d3 nearby enemies in a group)</b> — The target is stunned (save ends)<br> <i>Limited use:</i> The remorhaz can use <i>trilling vibrations</i> only when the escalation die is odd.</p><p><i>Burrow:</i> As the standard monster ability, except the remorhaz only needs to roll 6+ in snow.</p><p><i>Massive heat absorption:</i> When a creature is engaged with the remorhaz at the start of its turn, it takes cold damage equal to twice the escalation die.</p><p><i>Shatterer:</i> Death can cause fluid-filled sacks inside the frost-würm to explode. When the attack roll that kills the frost-würm is a natural even roll, each nearby creature takes 20 cold damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>180</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Remorhaz Queen

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>11<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +2d10 (see <i>sluggish initiative</i>)</p><p><b>Bite and trample +17 vs. AC</b> — 80 damage, 40 fire damage, and the remorhaz grabs the target<br> <i>Miss:</i> The target and each other creature engaged with the remorhaz takes 20 fire damage.</p><p><b>R: Nova blast +16 vs. PD (1d3 nearby enemies)</b> — 100 fire damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 25 fire damage.</p><p><i>Burrow:</i> As the standard monster ability, except the remorhaz only needs to roll 6+ in snow and ice.</p><p><i>Furnace aura:</i> When a creature is engaged with the remorhaz (or grabbed by it) at the start of its turn, it takes fire damage equal to 10 × the escalation die.</p><p><i>Sluggish initiative:</i> The queen may be sluggish after eating unsuccessful suitors, laying eggs, or moving across the ice like a rushing avalanche. Roll 2d10 to determine her current initiative.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Bejeweled remorhaz:</i> The remorhaz has glowing “jewels” on its armored plates. When a nearby or far away enemy misses with an attack against the remorhaz, that enemy chooses one: It takes 25 fire damage; OR one piece of its non-magical equipment (something useful, GM’s choice) melts or burns up. Adjust skill checks or stats accordingly.</p><p><i>Remorhaz steamer:</i> The remorhaz is melting the ice/snow all the time and obscuring steam rises into the air. Ranged attacks against the remorhaz take a –2 penalty, or a –4 penalty if the attacker is far away.</p><p><i>Spiney remorhaz:</i> The remorhaz is covered in red-hot spines. When a nearby enemy rolls a natural 1–5 with an attack roll, it takes 30 fire damage unless it has somehow protected itself from the heat.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>27</b></p><p><b>26</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>580</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Rust Monster

### Rust Monster

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Aberration</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +5</p><p><b>Caustic bite +8 vs. AC (one creature wearing light armor or no armor)</b> — 10 damage, and 5 ongoing acid damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The target is now considered to be wearing no armor (the armor is damaged beyond repair; adjust defenses accordingly). If the target’s armor is magical, the target must roll a hard save (16+). On a success, the armor isn’t affected. This effect is permanent until the creature obtains new armor.</p><p><b>Rusting antenna +8 vs. PD (one creature wearing heavy armor)</b> — 1 damage, and the target is now considered to be wearing no armor (the armor is damaged beyond repair; adjust defenses accordingly). If the target’s armor is magical, the target must roll a hard save (16+). On a success, the armor isn’t affected. This effect is permanent until the creature obtains new armor.</p><p><i>Corrupting body:</i> Whenever a creature hits the rust monster with a melee weapon, the attacker must roll a save; on a failure, the weapon is destroyed. Magic weapons require an easy save (6+) instead. This effect is permanent.</p><p><i>Rust’s targets:</i> Magic items wielded by creatures with 60 hp or more are not affected by the rust monster’s ability to destroy items (but the target still takes damage).</p><p><i>Saving quirks:</i> Before rolling a save for a magic item, a PC can gain a +5 bonus to the save by agreeing to roleplay the item’s quirk as a huge element of their personality until the next full heal-up. Failure to live up to this roleplaying agreement means that the item hasn’t received the support it needs from its owner to survive the rust monster’s destructive effects, and the item is destroyed at the end of the next battle even if its owner successfully saved.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Big antenna:</i> When the rust monster scores a critical hit, it can try to destroy another random magic item in the target’s possession (or a random normal item if the target has no other magic items). The creature must roll a save for the item, as usual.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>45</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Rust Monster Obliterator

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Demon</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +8</p><p><b>Caustic bite +10 vs. AC (one creature wearing light armor or no armor)</b> — 18 damage, and 5 ongoing acid damage<br> <i>Natural 14+:</i> The target is now considered to be wearing no armor (the armor is damaged beyond repair; adjust defenses accordingly). If the target’s armor is magical, the target must roll a hard save (16+). On a success, the armor isn’t affected. This effect is permanent until the creature obtains new armor.</p><p><b>Rusting antenna +10 vs. PD (one creature wearing heavy armor)</b> — 10 damage, and the target is now considered to be wearing no armor (the armor is damaged beyond repair; adjust defenses accordingly). If the target’s armor is magical, the target must roll a hard save (16+). On a success, the armor isn’t affected. This effect is permanent until the creature obtains new armor.<br> Each time the rust monster obliterator destroys heavy armor with this attack, it gains a different random demon ability until the end of the battle (reroll duplicate abilities). (See the demon abilities table.)</p><p><i>Corrupting body:</i> Whenever a creature hits the rust monster with a melee weapon, the attacker must roll a save; on a failure, the weapon is destroyed. Magic weapons require an easy save (6+) instead. This effect is permanent.</p><p><i>Rust’s targets:</i> Magic items wielded by creatures with 100 hp or more are not affected by the rust monster’s ability to destroy items (but the target still takes damage).</p><p><i>Saving quirks:</i> Before rolling a save for a magic item, a PC can gain a +5 bonus to the save by agreeing to roleplay the item’s quirk as a huge element of their personality until the next full heal-up. Failure to live up to this roleplaying agreement means that the item hasn’t received the support it needs from its owner to survive the rust monster’s destructive effects, and the item is destroyed at the end of the next battle even if its owner saved.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Tail whirligig:</i> When an enemy targets the rust monster obliterator with a spell, the rust monster rolls a save. On a success, the spell has no effect on the rust monster. If the rust monster is staggered, it must roll a hard save (16+) instead.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>72</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Sahuagin

### Iron Sea Shark

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>2×</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +6</p><p><b>Massive iron jaws +10 vs. AC</b> — 14 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 2d6 damage.</p><p><i>Frenzy:</i> While staggered, if the iron sea shark is unengaged at the start of its turn, it must roll an easy save (6+). On a failure, the shark must move and attack a random nearby enemy that’s staggered, or a random nearby if there are no staggered enemies.</p><p><i>Shredder:</i> When an enemy misses with a melee attack against an iron sea shark and rolls a natural 1–5, the attacker takes 2d6 damage.</p><p><i>Water breather:</i> Sharks breathe underwater and swim very well. They’re not so good out of sea water (even if they jump), so treat them as semi-hazardous terrain while they’re busy thrashing to death outside the water.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>32</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Razor Shark

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>2<sup>nd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +6</p><p><b>Razortoothed jaws +7 vs. AC</b> — 4 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> Increase the damage by +1 for each razor shark mook that has dropped this battle.<br> <i>Natural even miss:</i> The target and the razor shark each take 1d6 damage.</p><p><i>Frenzy (group):</i> When two or more razor sharks in the same mob are dropped to 0 hp by an attack, as a free action each dropped razor shark attacks one random nearby non-razor shark creature before it dies. That creature takes 1d8 damage.</p><p><i>Water breather:</i> Sharks breathe underwater and swim very well. They’re not so good out of sea water (even if they jump), so treat them as semi-hazardous terrain while they’re busy thrashing to death outside the water.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>11</b></p><p><b>10</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Sahuagin

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9</p><p><b>Trident and bite +10 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 10 damage<br> <i>Natural 20:</i> Increase the escalation die by 1, and the target is hampered (<i>makes only basic attacks</i>) until the end of its next turn.</p><p><b>R: Barbed crossbow +9 vs. AC (one nearby enemy, or a far away enemy at –2 atk)</b> — 10 damage, and 5 ongoing damage</p><p><i>Blood frenzy:</i> Make a note of the escalation die when the sahuagin becomes staggered. The sahuagin gains a bonus to its melee attacks and damage equal to the escalation die value for the rest of the battle.</p><p><i>Water breather:</i> Sahuagin breathe underwater and swim very well.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Demon-touched: </i>Roll a d6 on the Demon Random Abilities table. The sahuagin gains that ability.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>70</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Sahuagin Glow Priest

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Caster</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +10</p><p><b>Coral rod +10 vs. AC</b> — 12 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The priest teleports the target next to one of its nearby allies that it can see, who engages it as a free action. It can’t teleport the target to a location that causes it direct damage (so into a pool of flaming oil is out, but off a ship into the sea is fine).</p><p><b>R: Glowpriest’s prayer +10 vs. MD (1d3 nearby enemies)</b> — 12 psychic damage, and if the attack hits 2 or more targets, roll 1d8 after the attack for the prayer’s effect<br> <i>1–2 (Hymn of hate):</i> One random nearby conscious enemy takes 4d6 negative energy damage.<br> <i>3–4 (Curse of despair):</i> Each target that was hit takes a –2 penalty (non-cumulative) to all saves until the end of the battle.<br> <i>5–6 (Scream of victory):</i> Until the start of the glowpriest’s next turn, each sahuagin and demon in the battle adds the escalation die to its attacks and the PCs don’t.<br> <i>7–8 (Word of refuge):</i> Remove the glowpriest from play. At the start of its next turn, return it to play nearby its original location. It gains a +4 bonus to all defenses until the end of its next turn after it returns to play.</p><p><i>Water breather:</i> Sahuagin breathe underwater and swim very well.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>70</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Sahuagin Mutant

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>6<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +12</p><p><b>Four-armed frenzy +11 vs. AC (1d4 attacks)</b> — 15 damage<br> <i>Natural 4, 8, 12, 16, 20:</i> The target takes 10 ongoing damage.</p><p><b>R: Heavy crossbow +10 vs. AC (one nearby or far away enemy)</b> — 30 damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The target takes 10 ongoing damage.</p><p><i>Limited escalator:</i> The sahuagin mutant adds the escalation die to its attacks until the die is 5+.</p><p><i>Water breather:</i> Sahuagin breathe underwater and swim very well.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Punisher:</i> When an enemy intercepts the sahuagin mutant, it takes 4d8 damage from the mutant’s claws and teeth.</p><p><i>Ripper:</i> When an enemy makes a melee attack against the sahuagin mutant and rolls a natural odd miss, that enemy takes 2d8 damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>200</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Sahuagin Raider

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>2<sup>nd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Troop</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +4</p><p><b>Coral-tipped spear +6 vs. AC</b> — 6 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit against a stuck or hampered enemy:</i> The target takes 1d6 extra damage.</p><p><b>R: Hooked net +6 vs. PD</b> — 3 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target is hampered (save ends).<br> <i>Natural odd hit:</i> The target is stuck (save ends).<br> <i>Limited use:</i> 1/battle.</p><p><i>Blood rage:</i> The sahuagin raider gains a +2 attack bonus while it’s staggered.</p><p><i>Water breather:</i> Sahuagin breathe underwater and swim very well.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>34</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## The Saved

### Avenging Orb

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>2<sup>nd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Caster</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +3</p><p><b>Gauntlet slap +5 vs. AC</b> — 3 damage<br> <i>Natural 5, 10, 15, 20:</i> The target also takes 3 ongoing psychic damage.</p><p><b>R: Orb of pain +7 vs. MD (one or more nearby or far away enemies; see <i>history of abuse</i>)</b> — 5 psychic damage<br> <i>Natural 5, 10, 15, 20:</i> The target also takes 3 ongoing psychic damage.</p><p><i>Beyond saving:</i> The avenging orb takes a –5 penalty to saving throws.</p><p><i>History of abuse:</i> Keep track of the number of enemy attacks that hit the avenging orb during the battle. Until the end of the battle, the avenging orb can target an additional enemy beyond the first with its <i>orb of pain</i> attack for each of those hits. (Note that avenging orbs engaged in melee usually choose to use <i>orb of pain</i> and suffer any resulting opportunity attacks; if they’re lucky they’ll survive the attack and be able to choose more targets for the <i>orb of pain</i>.)</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>46</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Destroying Sword

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>2<sup>nd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +4</p><p><b>Cheap greatsword +8 vs. AC</b> — 3 damage<br> <i>Natural odd hit:</i> The target takes extra damage equal to half the amount the destroying sword took from the last attack that hit it this battle.</p><p><b>R: Shortbow +6 vs. AC (one nearby or far away enemy)</b> — 6 damage</p><p><i>Beyond saving:</i> The destroying sword takes a –5 penalty to saving throws.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>38</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Enduring Shield

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>2<sup>nd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Blocker</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +3</p><p><b>Steel hammer +7 vs. AC</b> — 6 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 1d4 damage.</p><p><i>Anguished interceptor:</i> When an enduring shield is engaged and an enemy attempts to move past it, the enduring shield can roll a disengage check to intercept it as an interrupt action (once per round). If the attempt fails, the enduring shield takes 1d6 psychic damage.</p><p><i>Beyond saving:</i> The enduring shield takes a –5 penalty to saving throws.</p><p><i>Supernatural endurance:</i> When an attack hits the enduring shield, it gains a +5 bonus to the defense that the attack targeted until the end of the battle or until another attack hits it, in which case the bonus switches to the defense most recently hit.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>40</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Skeleton

For all skeletons

_Resist weapons 16+:_ When a weapon attack targets this creature, the attacker must roll a natural 16+ on the attack roll or it only deals half damage.

Also, the pitch of their wings is high and thin, allowing a stirge to get very close without tipping off its prey.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>One and done:</i> After hitting a living creature that has blood with its <i>draining probe</i> attack, the stirge heals 5 hit points and will use its next turn to move, fleeing to the hive to feed the stirgelings…and to alert the hive that there is an easy meal nearby. A new full-strength stirge enters the battle during the next round on the same initiative count.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>10</b></p><p><b>18</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Soul Flenser

### The Flensed

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>9<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Aberration</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +12</p><p><b>Fists, claws, or shoddy weapons +13 vs. AC</b> — 20 damage, or 40 damage against a target that currently has one or more powers <i>flensed</i> away.</p><p><i>Connection to the Oversoul:</i> When a creature slays one of the Flensed, it can roll a hard save (16+). If it succeeds, the creature regains one power it had <i>flensed</i> away.</p><p><i>Flensing escalator:</i> The Flensed gains an attack bonus equal to the escalation die against creatures that have had one or more powers flensed away.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>60</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Soul Flenser

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>9<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Aberration</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +15</p><p><b>Soul flensing tentacles +14 vs. PD</b> — 30 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit, or any hit against a weakened, stunned, or confused target:</i> Randomly select one of the target’s limited-use powers or spells. The soul flenser flenses it away, removing it from the target until that creature regains it via a successful connection to the oversoul (see below).<br> <i>Natural 3, 6, or 9:</i> The target is confused (save ends).</p><p><b>C: Soul blast +14 vs. MD (1d4 nearby enemies in a group)</b> — 35 psychic damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target is weakened (save ends).<br> <i>Natural odd hit:</i> If the target is already weakened, it’s also stunned until end of its next turn.<br> <i>Natural 3, 6, or 9:</i> The target is confused (save ends).</p><p><i>Connection to the Oversoul:</i> When a creature slays a soul flenser, it can roll a hard save (16+). If it succeeds, the creature regains one power it has had <i>flensed</i> away.</p><p><i>Intellect fortress:</i> When an enemy misses the soul flenser with an attack against MD, that attacker takes half the miss damage, if any.</p><p><i>Underkraken teleport:</i> A soul flenser that has successfully flensed at least once can (and usually will, provided some of its enemies are confused, weakened, or stunned) use a standard action to prepare itself to teleport. Once it does this, during its next turn it can use a move action to teleport back to its home underkraken, no matter how distant, leaving the battle behind. Soul flensers fighting beside or within their underkraken can’t use this ability; they’re already home.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Flensing escalator:</i> The soul flenser gains an attack bonus equal to the escalation die against creatures that have had one or more powers flensed away.</p><p><i>Oversoul control:</i> While confused by a soul flenser’s effect, a creature that has had a power flensed away can use and re-use that limited power against their erstwhile allies, if the GM sees how to use the power in a useful way.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>25</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>180</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Specter

Nastier Specials for all specters

_Aura of loss:_ The first time during a battle the specter is staggered, each nearby enemy with 30 hp or fewer is hampered until the end of the specter’s next turn. (9<sup>th</sup> level dread specter affects enemies with 60 hp or fewer.)

_Healing drain:_ When an enemy engaged with a specter heals, it heals only half the normal hit points, and the specter heals the other half (round down).

_Spectral evasion:_ Once per battle as a free action when an enemy attacks the specter, it can force the attacker to reroll the attack and use the result the specter prefers.

### Dread Specter

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>3×</b></p><p><b>9<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +12</p><p><b>Icy, life-draining touch +12 vs. PD</b> — 110 negative energy damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> Each enemy engaged with the specter (including the target) takes 20 negative energy damage.</p><p><b>R: Deathly stare +12 vs. MD (up to 2 nearby enemies)</b> — 75 negative energy damage</p><p><i>Phantom movement:</i> As a move action when the escalation die is odd, the specter can teleport anywhere nearby, dematerializing from its location to materialize in another.</p><p><i>Punishing aura:</i> When an enemy attacks the specter and misses, it takes 24 negative energy damage.</p><p><i>Wrack and ruin:</i> While a specter is in the battle, the PCs don’t add the escalation die to attack rolls, but it does.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Death grasp:</i> At the start of each of the specter’s turns, if any enemy in the battle has 60 hp or fewer, the specter can make a <i>death grasp</i> attack against one of those enemies as a free action. Be sure to let players see this one coming.</p><p><b>C: Death grasp +14 vs. MD (one nearby enemy with 60 hp or fewer)</b> — 60 negative energy damage</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>550</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Specter

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>2×</b></p><p><b>6<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9</p><p><b>Icy, life-draining touch +10 vs. PD</b> — 30 negative energy damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> Each enemy engaged with the specter (including the target) takes 4 negative energy damage.</p><p><b>R: Deathly stare +10 vs. MD</b> — 20 negative energy damage</p><p><i>Punishing aura:</i> When an enemy attacks the specter and misses, it takes 8 negative energy damage.</p><p><i>Wrack and ruin:</i> While a specter is in the battle, the PCs don’t add the escalation die to attack rolls, but it does.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>160</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Tarrasque

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Huge</b></p><p><b>15<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +20</p><p><span>Creature of Legend</span></p><p>The tarrasque can make one close attack and one melee attack each round as a standard action. Note that flying is usually no defense against the tarrasque, which is huge and powerful enough to pluck or whack enemies out of the sky with surprising leaps.</p><p><b>All-enveloping toothy maw +19 vs. AC</b> — 155 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The tarrasque grabs the target. It will swallow a grabbed enemy in 1d3 rounds (see <i>swallow whole</i>).<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The tarrasque swallows the target immediately (see <i>swallow whole</i>).</p><p><b>Immense spike, horn, or tusk +18 vs. AC</b> — 155 damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The target takes 9d6 extra damage and pops free from the tarrasque as it’s hurled far away.</p><p><b>C: Earth-shaking, taloned claw +20 vs. AC (each nearby enemy in a group)</b> — 155 damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The target is stunned (save ends).<br> <i>Miss:</i> The target is dazed (save ends).</p><p><b>C: Cataclysmic tail slam +18 vs. PD (each nearby enemy in a group)</b> — 170 damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The target is vulnerable (save ends).<br> <i>Miss:</i> The target is dazed until the end of its next turn.</p><p><i>Amphibious:</i> The tarrasque can swim and breathe underwater (or it holds so much air in its vast lungs that it makes no difference).</p><p><i>Enormously bulky:</i> The tarrasque is so huge that it ignores opportunity attacks. In addition, normal-sized enemies are like fleas to it, and disengaging from the tarrasque requires only an easy save (6+), unless the target is grabbed.</p><p><i>Immortal:</i> The tarrasque can’t be killed, save by the explicit will of a god (and not some jumped-up local god, either) or, perhaps, the sacrifice of a great icon. The tarrasque’s HP total indicates the amount of damage required to make it disgorge swallowed enemies and flee to go hibernate while it regenerates the damage it suffered and decide if it wants to rampage again.</p><p><i>Inflexible:</i> The tarrasque can’t easily fight foes that get onto its back, and may not even notice them if they aren’t attacking it. When it does tire of a passenger, it can either use its <i>tail slam</i> attack (–2 attack penalty: on a hit, the target only takes half damage and is knocked off the tarrasque [possibly falling damage]; on a miss, the target takes no damage) or a <i>drag</i> attack as a standard action, crushing the rider between its shell and a mountainside or other high, hard obstacle.</p><p><b>Drag +21 vs. PD (each creature on its back)</b> — 130 damage, the target pops free of the tarrasque, and the target is hampered (save ends)</p><p><i>Legendary resistance:</i> The tarrasque is immune to normal conditions and effects (stunned, weakened, etc.), but it isn’t completely impervious. Bypassing its resistances requires icon-supported effort. A PC can use one 5 or 6 they acquired from icon relationship dice rolls to overcome the resistance each time they use an attack or power that would apply a condition or effect upon the tarrasque. Of course, they must also provide a story to go along with the reason the tarrasque is affected.</p><p><i>Leveler:</i> When the escalation die is even, as a move action the tarrasque can demolish any ordinary structure it can reach, such as a house, castle wall, temple, or ship. The beast automatically reduces the structure to rubble, rendering it useless. Each creature on top of or within the structure is subject to a <i>collapse</i> attack.</p><p><b>Collapse +18 vs. PD (each creature in/on the structure)</b> — 90 damage, and the target is stuck and takes 20 ongoing damage (hard save ends both, 16+)</p><p><i>Swallow whole:</i> Once a creature is swallowed, it goes inside one of the tarrasque’s gigantic stomachs. It can still act while inside the tarrasque, but it will have to deal with the beast’s stomach acid that is splashing around. A swallowed creature must deal 400 damage to the tarrasque to force it to disgorge the contents of its gullet, freeing the creature. During the tarrasque’s turn, it can make a <i>gullet digestion</i> attack against the target as a free action.</p><p><b>Gullet digestion +19 vs. PD</b> — 80 acid damage, and 20 ongoing acid damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 5d12 acid damage.</p><p><i>Soft-ish innerbelly:</i> The tarrasque doesn’t have scales on the inside. It takes a –5 penalty to all defenses against attacks from inside its gullet, though only melee and close attacks can be made in there. The tarrasque’s insides are immune to acid damage, however.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Fear:</i> While engaged with the tarrasque, enemies that have 216 hp or fewer are dazed (–4 attack) and do not add the escalation die to their attacks.</p><p><i>Regeneration 230:</i> While a tarrasque is damaged, its malign magical flesh heals 230 hit points at the start of the tarrasque’s turn. It can regenerate five times per battle. If it heals up to its maximum hit points, then that use of <i>regeneration</i> doesn’t count against the five-use limit. With this power, the monstrosity is likely unstoppable without a powerful magical artifact designed specifically to bind, wound, or otherwise hamper the tarrasque.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>31</b></p><p><b>29</b></p><p><b>25</b></p><p><b>2130</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Treant

All treants except awakened tress have the _demolish_ ability.

_Free-form ability — Demolish:_ Given time, treants are capable of pulling apart just about anything that’s been put together. Their roots squeeze into spaces between paving stones, slowly pulling them up and out of place. Their branches can likewise worm their way into spaces in walls, doors, and gates, and with steady pressure they can pull down most human-made structures. This slow-motion destruction takes minutes for the simplest efforts and hours for major demolition.

### Awakened Trees

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Plant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +5<br>Vulnerability: fire</p><p><b>Lashing branches +9 vs. AC</b> — 7 damage</p><p><i>Hardwood resistance:</i> This creature has <i>resist damage 12+</i> to all damage except fire damage and melee weapon damage, which damages it normally.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>13</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Common Treant

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Plant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +4<br>Vulnerability: fire</p><p><b>Grasping branches +10 vs. AC</b> — 9 damage, and the treant grabs the target. When the treant starts its turn grabbing an enemy, it can make a <i>twist and snap</i> attack against that target as a standard action that turn.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>Twist and snap +14 (includes +4 grab bonus) vs. PD</b> — 27 damage</p><p><i>Fire fire fire!:</i> When the treant takes 15 or more fire damage from a single attack, it releases all grabbed creatures.</p><p><i>Hardwood resistance:</i> This creature has <i>resist damage 12+</i> to all damage except fire damage and melee weapon damage, which damages it normally.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Toxic haze:</i> The treant exudes a toxic cloud of pollen. When an enemy engages the treant or starts its turn engaged with the treant, it takes 4 poison damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>65</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Treant Titan

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>10<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Plant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9<br>Vulnerability: fire</p><p><b>Grasping branches +15 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 30 damage, and the treant grabs the target. When the treant starts its turn grabbing an enemy, it can make a <i>twist and snap</i> attack against that target as a standard action that turn.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>Twist and snap +19 (includes +4 grab bonus) vs. PD</b> — 80 damage, and the target is dazed (save ends). If the treant starts its turn grabbing a dazed enemy, it can make a <i>titanic rend</i> attack against that target as a standard action that turn.<br> <i>Miss:</i> 40 damage.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>Titanic rend +19 (includes +4 grab bonus) vs. PD</b> — 160 damage, and the treant titan can continue making <i>titanic rend</i> attacks against the target until it escapes the grab, at which point the treant will have to use a <i>grasping branches</i> attack against it again.<br> <i>Miss:</i> 60 damage.</p><p><i>Fire fire fire!:</i> When the treant takes 35 or more fire damage from a single attack, it releases all grabbed creatures.</p><p><i>Hardwood resistance:</i> This creature has <i>resist damage 18+</i> to all damage except fire damage and melee weapon damage, which damages it normally.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Coffin of living wood:</i> When the treant titan hits with a <i>titanic rend</i> attack, the target is pulled into a hollow chamber within the treant. While grabbed by the treant this way, the target can’t be the target of its allies’ powers or spells.</p><p><i>Gauntlet of branches:</i> Countless smaller branches whip through the air around the treant titan. When a creature engaged with the treant misses it with an attack, that creature takes 12 damage from the whipping branches.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>28</b></p><p><b>26</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>390</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Troglodyte

For all troglodytes

_Trog stench:_ Trogs spray scents that stink so badly that other humanoids take penalties to all attacks, defenses, and saves when engaged with a troglodyte or when nearby three or more troglodytes. Non-humanoids aren’t affected.  
 Humanoids affected by _trog stench_ can make a normal save (with a penalty) at the end of each of their turns. If the save succeeds, the humanoid can ignore all _trog stench_ for the rest of the battle.  
 _Trog stench_ penalties vary for different humanoid races:

| Race | Save Penalty |
| --- | --- |
| Elves, gnolls, gnomes | –4 |
| Humans, halflings, half-elves, holy ones, tieflings, almost everyone else | –3 |
| Half-orcs, dragonics | –2 |
| Dwarves | –1 |
| Forgeborn | 0 |

### Trog

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>2<sup>nd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +4</p><p><b>Club +6 vs. AC</b> — 8 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> Damage equal to the penalty the trog’s stench currently imposes on the target.</p><p><b>R: Javelin +5 vs. AC</b> — 6 damage</p><p><i>Chameleon:</i> Underground, or in swamps and rivers, attacks against troglodytes by enemies who aren’t engaged with them take a –4 penalty.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>38</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Trog Underling

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>8<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +10</p><p><b>Club +12 vs. AC</b> — 22 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> Damage equal to three times the penalty the trog’s stench currently imposes on the target.</p><p><b>R: Javelin +11 vs. AC</b> — 16 damage</p><p><i>Chameleon:</i> Underground, or in swamps and rivers, attacks against troglodytes by enemies who aren’t engaged with them take a –4 penalty.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>38</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Troll

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Troop</b></p><p><b>Giant</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9</p><p><b>Greedy wicked claw +8 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 15 damage</p><p><i>Trollish regeneration 10: </i>While a troll is damaged, its rubbery flesh heals 10 hit points at the start of the troll’s turn. It can regenerate five times per battle. If it heals to its maximum hit points, then that use of <i>regeneration</i> doesn’t count against the five-use limit.<br> When the troll is hit by an attack that deals fire or acid damage, it loses one use of its <i>regeneration</i>, and it can’t regenerate during its next turn.<br> Dropping a troll to 0 hp doesn’t kill it if it has any uses of <i>regeneration</i> left.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Increased regeneration:</i> Increase the troll’s regeneration dice; the baseline amount a troll regenerates should run about 1/9 of its total hp, but you can go higher to be nasty.</p><p><i>Mutant:</i> Fire and acid don’t hurt the troll’s regeneration; lightning does instead.</p><p><i>Rending:</i> If both <i>claw</i> attacks hit the same target, the target also takes 10 ongoing damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>90</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Vampire

### Spawn of the Master
