### Vampire

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>10<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +15<br>Vulnerability: holy</p><p><b>Deathly touch +15 vs. PD</b> — 50 negative energy damage<br> <i>Natural 11+:</i> The target is also weakened until the end of its next turn (–4 attacks and defenses). In addition, the target expends one unused limited trait (a spell, power, or talent with a once-per-battle or daily use, but not magic item powers) of its choice.</p><p><i>Vampiric regeneration:</i> The vampire regenerates 1 hp per level at the start of each round indefinitely, but it turns to mist if it drops to 0 hp (see below).</p><p><i>Mist form:</i> Unless it is slain in a manner appropriate for truly killing vampires in the campaign, a vampire that drops to 0 hp drifts away to return and fight some other day.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><b>C: Vampiric compulsion +15 vs. MD (one enemy; see below)</b> — The target is confused and vulnerable (save ends)<br> <i>Limited use:</i> The vampire can use <i>vampiric compulsion</i> as a free action only when a nearby enemy attacks the vampire and misses with a natural attack roll of 1–5.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>26</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>26</b></p><p><b>220</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Vampire Spawn

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>6<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +10<br>Vulnerability: holy</p><p><b>Claw +10 vs. AC</b> — 18 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The vampire spawn can make a <i>fangs</i> attack against the target as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>Fangs +14 vs. AC</b> — 7 damage, and a humanoid target is weakened (–4 attack and defenses) until the end of the vampire spawn’s next turn</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>90</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

Warbanners have a number of abilities in common. The feral warbanner has the full version of these abilities. You may customize the feral warbanner by giving it icon-associated abilities.

A warbanner generally commands large groups of mooks that are simple to play. Creatures in a warbanner’s band are allies fully under its control. It could also have allies not in its band.

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>2×</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Caster</b></p><p><b>Construct</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +8</p><p><b>Flagspear +9 vs. AC</b> — 18 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 8 damage.</p><p><b>C: Banner magic</b> — Roll 2d20 and use each roll (or a lower result of your choice) to determine one effect<br> <i>1–5:</i> The warbanner’s bearer can make a basic attack with a +2 attack bonus as a free action.<br> <i>6–10:</i> Add a 3rd level orc mook to the warbanner’s band.<br> <i>11–15:</i> The warbanner can make a <i>flagspear</i> attack as a free action.<br> <i>16–20:</i> The warbanner can make a <i>false rally</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: False rally +8 vs. MD (one nearby enemy with 15 hp or fewer)</b> — The target is confused (hard save ends, 16+)<br> <i>Critical hit:</i> The target can now only save against the confusion with a natural 20 (or until the warbanner drops) and can’t flee if the rest of the PCs choose to do so.</p><p><i>Designated bearer:</i> Once per round as a quick action, the warbanner can fly directly above a lower-level ally in its band and designate that ally as its bearer. Alternately, it can release itself from a bearer and fly free.</p><p><i>Bearer beware:</i> While the warbanner has a bearer it moves with the bearer and is engaged by enemies that engage the bearer. The bearer is vulnerable to all attacks but it can use the escalation die.</p><p><i>Conditional resist damage 16+:</i> As feral warbanner.</p><p><i>Flight:</i> As feral warbanner.</p><p><i>Mook morale:</i> Mooks fighting in the warbanner’s band gain a bonus to their hit points equal to the warbanner’s level (3).</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>100</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>2×</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Caster</b></p><p><b>Construct</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9</p><p><b>Bladed fringe +8 vs. AC</b> — 15 damage, and 10 ongoing negative energy damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 10 damage.</p><p><b>C: Banner magic</b> — Roll 2d20 and use each roll (or a lower result of your choice) to determine one effect<br> <i>1–5:</i> The warbanner’s bearer can make a basic attack with a +2 attack bonus as a free action.<br> <i>6–10:</i> Each different enemy engaged with a creature in the warbanner’s band takes 1d10 psychic damage.<br> <i>11–15:</i> If any mooks in the warbanner’s band have dropped this battle, return one of those mooks to the battle next to the warbanner. (If the warbanner has no mooks in its band, choose a lower result.)<br> <i>16–20:</i> The warbanner can make a <i>false rally</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: False rally +9 vs. MD (one nearby enemy with 18 hp or fewer)</b> — The target is confused (hard save ends, 16+)<br> <i>Critical hit:</i> The target can now only save against the confusion with a natural 20 (or until the warbanner drops) and can’t flee if the rest of the PCs choose to do so.</p><p><i>Designated bearer:</i> Once per round as a quick action, the warbanner can fly directly above a lower-level ally in its band and designate that ally as its bearer. Alternately, it can release itself from a bearer and fly free.</p><p><i>Bearer beware:</i> While the warbanner has a bearer it moves with the bearer and is engaged by enemies that engage the bearer. The bearer is vulnerable to all attacks but it can use the escalation die.</p><p><i>Conditional resist damage 16+:</i> As feral warbanner.</p><p><i>Flight:</i> As feral warbanner.</p><p><i>Mook morale:</i> Mooks fighting in the warbanner’s band gain a bonus to their hit points equal to the warbanner’s level (4).</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>104</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>2×</b></p><p><b>2<sup>nd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Caster</b></p><p><b>Construct</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +7</p><p><b>Whipping barbed tassel +7 vs. AC</b> — 10 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 5 damage.</p><p><b>C: Banner magic</b> — Roll 2d20 and use each roll (or a lower result of your choice) to determine one effect<br> <i>1–5:</i> The warbanner’s bearer can make a basic attack with a +2 attack bonus as a free action.<br> <i>6–10:</i> Each different enemy engaged with a creature in the warbanner’s band takes 1d6 psychic damage.<br> <i>11–15:</i> If any mooks in the warbanner’s band have dropped this battle, return one of those mooks to the battle next to the warbanner. (If the warbanner has no mooks in its band, choose a lower result.)<br> <i>16–20:</i> The warbanner can make a <i>false rally</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>C: False rally +7 vs. MD (one nearby enemy with 12 hp or fewer)</b> — The target is confused (hard save ends, 16+)<br> <i>Critical hit:</i> The target can now only save against the confusion with a natural 20 (or until the warbanner drops) and can’t flee if the rest of the PCs choose to do so.</p><p><i>Designated bearer:</i> Once per round as a quick action, the warbanner can fly directly above a lower-level ally in its band and designate that ally as its bearer. Alternately, it can release itself from a bearer and fly free.</p><p><i>Bearer beware:</i> While the warbanner has a bearer it moves with the bearer and is engaged by enemies that engage the bearer. The bearer is vulnerable to all attacks but it can use the escalation die.</p><p><i>Conditional resist damage 16+:</i> Unless an ally in the warbanner’s band dropped to 0 hp since the start of the current round, an enemy attacking the warbanner must roll a natural 16+ on the attack roll or it only takes half damage. This ability has no effect if the warbanner has no allies in its band.</p><p><i>Flight:</i> Warbanners fly quickly, fluttering in winds only they can feel, preferably never touching the ground. They can’t fly off the ground higher than a flag on a pole can be carried into battle, so enemies on the ground can still target them. At best, a warbanner might gain a +2 bonus to defenses against attacks made by small PCs like halflings and gnomes.</p><p><i>Mook morale:</i> Mooks fighting in the warbanner’s band gain a bonus to their hit points equal to the warbanner’s level (2).</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>70</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Wendigo

### Elder Wendigo

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Huge</b></p><p><b>9<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Demon</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +18</p><p><b>Icy claws +14 vs. PD (3 attacks, each against a different nearby enemy)</b> — 50 cold damage<br> <i>Frostburn:</i> If all three attacks hit, each nearby enemy takes 4d10 fire damage.</p><p><b>C: Flame blizzard +14 vs. PD (1d6 nearby or far away enemies, but not more than esc. die)</b> — 90 fire or cold damage (GM choice)<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target is hampered until the end of its next turn.</p><p><b>C: Horrific gaze +14 vs. MD (one nearby or far away enemy)</b> — 120 psychic damage, and the target is confused (save ends)<br> <i>Fourth failed confusion save:</i> The target slips into madness and becomes a cannibal cultist or wendigo or some other terrible demon-thing of the GM’s or player’s choice in 2d10 hours.<br> <i>Miss:</i> 60 psychic damage.</p><p><i>Flight:</i> The elder wendigo can walk on the wind. It is not a graceful flyer, but it moves as fast as the wind that carries it.</p><p><i>Swirling snow and fog and flame:</i> The elder wendigo gains a +5 bonus to all defenses against attacks by far away enemies.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Force of disruption:</i> When the elder wendigo scores a critical hit against a target or drops a target to 0 hp or lower, that creature must permanently change one of its icon relationship points to a relationship with a different icon—one of a few that the GM chooses. Alternatively, a point the character already has with one of those icons changes to involve another icon (of the PC’s choice).</p><p><i>The demon stares back:</i> Once per round when a nearby or far away enemy attacks the elder wendigo and rolls a natural odd miss, the wendigo can make a <i>horrific gaze</i> attack against that attacker as a free action.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>26</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>600</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Ravenous Cannibal

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Humanoid</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +9</p><p><b>Bloody melee weapon +9 vs. AC</b> — 4 damage, and 4 ongoing damage</p><p><b>Latching bite +9 vs. AC (one staggered enemy, or one enemy making saving throw rolls)</b> — 6 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> Add another ravenous cannibal mook to the mob (it must have been hiding somewhere nearby, or wasn’t really dead when it dropped earlier in the battle).</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>11</b></p><p><b>13</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Wendigo Spirit

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +12</p><p><b>Soul bite +10 vs. MD</b> — 36 psychic damage, and the target is affected by <i>wendigo’s hunger</i> (save ends)<br> <i>Wendigo’s hunger:</i> Until the target saves, roll 1d6 at the start of each of its turns. It takes the corresponding action for its full turn instead of its normal turn:<br> <i>1–2:</i> The target takes 10 damage as it bites itself.<br> <i>3–4:</i> The target makes a basic attack against its nearest or most vulnerable ally (moving to that target if necessary).<br> <i>5–6:</i> The target attacks the wendigo if it can; otherwise, it does nothing.</p><p><b>Wind claw +10 vs. PD (2 attacks)</b> — 15 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> After the attack the wendigo can teleport somewhere nearby as a free action.</p><p><i>Flight:</i> The wendigo can walk on the wind. It is not a graceful flyer, but it moves as fast as the wind that carries it. Nearby creatures can see its feet blazing with fire as it runs.</p><p><i>Spirit form:</i> The wendigo has <i>resist damage 16+</i> to all damage except thunder damage. A wendigo spirit can move through solid objects but it can’t end its movement inside them.</p><p><i>Unseen horror:</i> The wendigo is invisible to far away creatures. When the wendigo attacks, if its target couldn’t see it at the start of its turn, the wendigo gains a +2 attack bonus that turn.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Curse of the wendigo:</i> If a creature subject to <i>wendigo’s hunger</i> drops itself (through biting) or an ally (with a basic attack) to 0 hp or lower, that creature also begins making last gasp saves. Failing the fourth last gasp save turns the creature into a raving cannibal; it loses all its normal abilities and becomes an NPC until the PCs find a way to restore their ally (at GM’s discretion).</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>100</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Werebeasts

Each werebeast can take one of three forms as a quick action once per round: A humanoid form, a beast form, or a hybrid form that combines the two. The hybrid form is the most powerful in combat, but the humanoid and beast forms are useful for various activities outside of combat as well.

The stats below work for the beast and hybrid forms. If a werebeast ends up fighting in humanoid form, subtract 2 from all its defenses and halve its normal attack damage.

The following powers are common for werebeasts.

_Beast heart (all three forms):_ Animals of the werebeast’s type are intuitively on good terms with the were, even dire animals. If the werebeast betrays them, however, retaliation is certain and merciless.

_Cursed bite (hybrid or animal form only):_ While the moon is full, the first time each battle a creature takes damage from a werebeast melee attack, it takes 10 extra damage (champion: 20 damage; epic: 40 damage). The malignant curse, transmitted through the attack, shocks the mortal flesh. Further attacks, even from weres of different types, don’t cause extra damage. Unless blessed, purged, or otherwise cured, the damaged creature will turn into a werebeast on the night of the next full moon. Heroes powerful enough to fight werebeasts can usually find benefactors or rituals to cure them, but there’s an exception to every rule. GM, if you’re unsure whether it’s a full moon, roll a d10. On a 1–3, the moon is full enough.

_Resilient shifting (all three forms):_ As mentioned above, a werebeast can shift forms once per round as a quick action. When a werebeast shifts, it can roll a save against one save ends effect.

Nastier Specials for all werebeasts

The following ability is extremely nasty when combined with the _bestial fury_ most werebeasts have. It’s possibly better used as a story option, a consequence of a problem with a skill check or an icon relationship, or a situation that should have been avoided and may require sacrifices to deal with:

_Moon fury (hybrid form only):_ While fighting in moonlight, a werebeast gains a bonus to damage equal to its level (champion: double its level; epic: triple it).

### Werebear

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Large</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Troop</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +10</p><p><b>Massive claws +10 vs. AC</b> — 20 damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The werebear grabs the target. As a standard action, it can make a <i>head chomp</i> attack against an enemy it’s grabbing.</p><p><i>[Special trigger]</i> <b>Head chomp +14 (includes +4 grab bonus) vs. AC (one enemy it’s grabbing)</b> — 70 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 20 damage.</p><p><i>Bestial fury (hybrid form only):</i> Werebears gain a bonus to damage equal to the escalation die (champion: double the die; epic: quadruple the die).</p><p><i>Unnatural vigor (hybrid or animal form only):</i> When the werebear is not staggered at the start of its turn, it heals 20 hp.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Chew on arm:</i> Instead of chomping on a grabbed enemy’s head, the werebear can make an <i>arm crunch</i> attack against an enemy it’s grabbing.</p><p><b>Arm crunch +14 vs. AC</b> — 70 damage, and the target is weakened until it regains maximum hit points</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>21</b></p><p><b>140</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Wereboar

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>2×</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Troop</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +7</p><p><b>Goring tusks +9 vs. AC (1d3 enemies)</b> — 15 damage</p><p><i>Slashing tusks:</i> While the escalation die is 3+, the crit range of this attack expands by 2.</p><p><i>Beastly grit:</i> When the wereboar takes 8 damage or less from any source, it takes no damage instead.</p><p><i>Bestial durability:</i> The wereboar can roll normal saves against effects that aren’t save ends (until end of turn or battle, for example).</p><p><i>Bestial fury (hybrid form only):</i> Wereboars gain a bonus to damage equal to the escalation die (champion: double the die; epic: quadruple the die).</p><p><i>Unnatural vigor (hybrid or animal form only):</i> When the wereboar is not staggered at the start of its turn, it heals 18 hp.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Vicious turn:</i> Once per battle, the wereboar can make a <i>smash</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><b>Smash +9 vs. PD</b> — The target is dazed (save ends)</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>16</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>120</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Wererat

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>2<sup>nd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Troop</b></p><p><b>Beast</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +11</p><p><b>Infected bite +7 vs. AC</b> — 2 damage and 2 ongoing damage, and the crit range for each wererat in the battle against the target expands by 1 (cumulative)<br> <i>Natural 11+:</i> The target can’t make opportunity attacks until the end of the turn (making it easier for the wererat to move away from the target).<br> <i>Hybrid miss:</i> While in hybrid form, when the wererat makes an opportunity attack with <i>infected bite</i>, it deals damage equal to its level on a miss.</p><p><i>Unnatural vigor (hybrid or animal form only):</i> When the wererat is not staggered at the start of its turn, it heals 5 hp.</p><p><i>Bestial fury (hybrid form only):</i> Wererats gain a bonus to damage equal to the escalation die (champion: double the die; epic: quadruple the die).</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Uncanny moves:</i> The wererat takes no damage and suffers no effects from attacks that miss.</p><p><i>Piercing shriek:</i> Once per battle when the escalation die is 2+ and there are three or more wererats in the battle, a wererat can make a <i>piercing shriek</i> attack as a free action. Usually all the wererats in the battle will do this at the same time.</p><p><b>C: Piercing shriek +7 vs. MD (the closest nearby enemy)</b> — 4 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 2 damage.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>18</b></p><p><b>34</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Weretiger

### Werewolf

## Whispering Prophet

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>5<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Leader</b></p><p><b>Aberration</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +15</p><p><b>Tentacle caress +9 vs. PD</b> — 12 damage, and the target is vulnerable to psychic damage (save ends)</p><p><b>C: Whispered secrets +10 vs. MD (1d3 nearby enemies)</b> — 5 psychic damage, and the target’s mind is filled with a delusional scene from its past that depends on the roll<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target is confused until the end of its next turn as it sees a foe from its past.<br> <i>Natural odd hit:</i> The target is weakened until the end of its next turn as it remembers a past failure.<br> <i>Rewards of the patron:</i> So long as the attack hits one or more targets, one ally of the prophet’s choice gains a cumulative +1 attack bonus until the end of the battle that increases that ally’s natural attack roll (so a roll of natural 15 becomes a roll of natural 16 with a +1 bonus, or a natural 17 with a +2 bonus, etc.). The ally can choose not to use the bonus.</p><p><i>Saw it coming:</i> Twice per battle as a free action, the prophet can try to avoid a non-critical attack that hits it. The attacker must reroll the attack roll with a –4 penalty.</p><p><i>Knows the angles:</i> Twice per battle as a move action, the prophet can teleport to anywhere it can see, or to a location it can’t see but that has the correct geometry and that it has previously prepared (a lair).</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Haruspicy master:</i> When an enemy has dropped to 0 hp or lower since the prophet’s last turn, as a quick action it can get a glimpse of the near-future. It grants 1d3 nearby allies a +4 bonus to attacks and to all defenses until the start of its next turn.</p><p><i>A special secret:</i> When the prophet makes a <i>whispered secrets</i> attack, it can choose to target only one nearby enemy. If it does, it gains a +4 attack bonus against that enemy and the hit effects are save ends.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>20</b></p><p><b>62</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Wibble

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>1<sup>st</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Construct</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +1</p><p><b>R: Force burp spell +6 vs. PD</b> — 4 force damage</p><p><i>Disengaged:</i> Wibbles gain a +5 bonus to disengage checks. They also don’t remain engaged with their foes and will move every turn in battle. When they fail a disengage check, a wibble moves away anyway.</p><p><i>Eruptive blorp:</i> When an enemy hits a wibble with a melee attack, it takes force damage equal to its level.</p><p><i>Flight:</i> Wibbles waft about. They can fly well enough to ignore most wind, but not strong gale winds.</p><p><i>Whiff and wibble:</i> When a creature makes a non-spell attack against a wibble and rolls a natural 1–2, 1d3 new wibbles are created in the same area. These new wibbles typically melt back into their “parent” at the end of a battle if not destroyed, but sometimes they remain separate and drift off on their own.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>6</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

The zombie takes 1d6 damage</p><p><i>Headshot:</i> The first time an enemy crits the zombie, the beast must roll a save. If it succeeds, it takes normal crit damage. If it fails, it drops to 0 hp. ### Zombie of the Silver Rose

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>4<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +7</p><p><b>Iron-hard hands +9 vs. AC</b> — 7 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> Both the zombie and its target take 1d6 damage.</p><p><i>Hand of the fallen:</i> When a melee attack drops one or more Silver Rose mooks, the hand of one of those zombies ends up severed from its owner and latched onto a nearby enemy. The afflicted creature is vulnerable to all attacks until the hand is removed, which takes a standard action by that creature or an ally next to them.</p><p><i>Shot to the head:</i> When an attack drops this zombie and it had 2, 4, or 6 hp remaining, the attack deals the same amount of damage to another member of the mob. If this zombie has any other number of hit points left? No hit to the head.</p><p><span>Nastier Specials</span></p><p><i>Curse of failure:</i> Each round, one zombie mook in the Silver Rose mob can make a <i>curse</i> attack as a quick action.</p><p><b>C: Curse +4 vs. MD (one nearby enemy)</b> — The target is weakened until the start of the zombie’s next turn<br> <i>Mob rule:</i> The <i>curse</i> gains an attack bonus equal to the number of Silver Rose zombies in the battle.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>15</b></p><p><b>11</b></p><p><b>20</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Zombie Shuffler

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>1<sup>st</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Mook</b></p><p><b>Undead</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +0<br>Vulnerability: holy</p><p><b>Rotting fist +5 vs. AC</b> — 3 damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> Both the zombie and its target take 1d4 damage!</p><p><i>Headshot:</i> A critical hit against a zombie shuffler deals triple damage instead of the normal double damage for a crit.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>14</b></p><p><b>12</b></p><p><b>8</b></p><p><b>10</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Zorigami

### Apex Zorigami

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>6<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Construct</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +11</p><p><b>Multi-geared mace +11 vs. AC</b> — 20 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit or miss:</i> The target can’t use the bonuses and powers of one of its randomly determined true magic items until the end of the battle.</p><p><b>R: Spray of sharpened gears +11 vs. AC (1d3 nearby enemies or one far away enemy)</b> — 15 damage<br> <i>Miss:</i> 8 damage.</p><p><i>Lethal parries:</i> When an enemy engaged with the apex zorigami misses it with an attack, the apex zorigami rolls a normal save; on a success, it can make a <i>multi-geared mace</i> attack as a free action.</p><p><i>Take five:</i> The escalation die does not increase the round after an apex zorigami is staggered or drops to 0 hp.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>24</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>19</b></p><p><b>75</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Dawn Zorigami

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>3<sup>rd</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Spoiler</b></p><p><b>Construct</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +6</p><p><b>Headbutt +8 vs. AC</b> — 10 damage, and the target moves down 1d6 points in initiative order</p><p><b>R: Ray of wasted time +8 vs. MD (1d3 nearby enemies or one far away enemy)</b> — 5 psychic damage, and 5 ongoing psychic damage<br> <i>Natural 16+:</i> The target also moves down 1d6 points in initiative order.</p><p><i>A moment of silence:</i> The escalation die does not increase the round after a dawn zorigami drops to 0 hp.</p><p><i>On pause:</i> A creature that is reduced to a negative initiative count in a battle involving one or more dawn zorigami moves forward in time, reappearing somewhere nearby in a number of minutes equal to their negative initiative count, presumably long after the current battle is over. The target may be confused by this effect, since the ways of zorigami are mysterious.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>22</b></p><p><b>13</b></p><p><b>17</b></p><p><b>30</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

### Dusk Zorigami

<table><tbody><tr><td><p><b>Normal</b></p><p><b>10<sup>th</sup>&nbsp;level</b></p><p><b>Wrecker</b></p><p><b>Construct</b></p></td><td><p>Initiative: +18</p><p><b>Arm full of blades +15 vs. AC (2 attacks)</b> — 30 damage<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The target is hampered (save ends).<br> <i>Natural odd hit:</i> The target can’t heal using its own recoveries (save ends).<br> <i>Natural 1–5:</i> The dusk zorigami can make a <i>shaking the hourglass</i> attack against a single target as a free action.</p><p><b>C: Shaking the hourglass +15 vs. MD (each nearby enemy not engaged with a zorigami)</b> — 20 psychic damage, and the target is vulnerable (save ends)<br> <i>Natural even hit:</i> The escalation die increases by one.<br> <i>Natural odd hit:</i> The escalation die decreases by one.</p><p><i>The ticking clock of its own mortality:</i> While it’s staggered, the dusk zorigami uses the escalation die.</p></td><td><p><b>AC</b></p><p><b>PD</b></p><p><b>MD</b></p><p><b>HP</b></p></td><td><p><b>28</b></p><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>23</b></p><p><b>200</b></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Underkrakens

While not monsters in and of themselves, underkrakens are enormous, city-sized dungeons in which monsters (like soul flensers) abide. They may be alive, or they may be complex vehicles, or colonies from another dimension or unknown portion of the world.
